<h2><span id="A" class="mw-headline">A</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Abductive logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abductive_logic_programming">Abductive logic programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Abductive logic programming (ALP) is a high-level knowledge-representation framework that can be used to solve problems declaratively based on abductive reasoning. It extends normal logic programming by allowing some predicates to be incompletely defined, declared as abducible predicates.</li>
<li><a title="Abductive reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abductive_reasoning">Abductive reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also called abduction,&nbsp;abductive inference,&nbsp;or retroduction) is a form of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Logical inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_inference">logical inference</a>&nbsp;which starts with an observation or set of observations then seeks to find the simplest and most likely explanation. This process, unlike&nbsp;<a title="Deductive reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deductive_reasoning">deductive reasoning</a>, yields a plausible conclusion but does not&nbsp;<a title="Logical positivism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_positivism">positively verify</a>&nbsp;it.</li>
<li><a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">Abstract data type</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical model</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">data types</a>, where a data type is defined by its behavior (<a title="Semantics (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantics_(computer_science)">semantics</a>) from the point of view of a&nbsp;<em>user</em>&nbsp;of the data, specifically in terms of possible values, possible operations on data of this type, and the behavior of these operations.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Abstraction (software engineering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstraction_(software_engineering)">Abstraction</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process of removing physical, spatial, or temporal details&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Attribute (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attribute_(computing)">attributes</a>&nbsp;in the study of objects or&nbsp;<a title="System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System">systems</a>&nbsp;in order to more closely attend to other details of interest</li>
<li><a title="Accelerating change" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accelerating_change">Accelerating change</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a perceived increase in the rate of&nbsp;<a title="Technological change" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_change">technological change</a>&nbsp;throughout history, which may suggest faster and more profound change in the future and may or may not be accompanied by equally profound social and cultural change.</li>
<li><a title="Action language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Action_language">Action language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a language for specifying&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="State transition system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_transition_system">state transition systems</a>, and is commonly used to create&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_model">formal models</a>&nbsp;of the effects of actions on the world.&nbsp;Action languages are commonly used in the&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">robotics</a>&nbsp;domains, where they describe how actions affect the states of systems over time, and may be used for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Automated planning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning">automated planning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Action model learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Action_model_learning">Action model learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an area of machine learning concerned with creation and modification of software agent's knowledge about effects and preconditions of the actions that can be executed within its environment. This knowledge is usually represented in logic-based action description language and used as the input for automated planners.</li>
<li><a title="Action selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Action_selection">Action selection</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a way of characterizing the most basic problem of intelligent systems: what to do next. In artificial intelligence and computational cognitive science, "the action selection problem" is typically associated with intelligent agents and animats&mdash;artificial systems that exhibit complex behaviour in an agent environment.</li>
<li><a title="Activation function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activation_function">Activation function</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>, the activation function of a node defines the output of that node given an input or set of inputs.</li>
<li><a title="Adaptive algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptive_algorithm">Adaptive algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; an algorithm that changes its behavior at the time it is run, based on&nbsp;<em>a priori</em>&nbsp;defined reward mechanism or criterion.</li>
<li><a title="Adaptive neuro fuzzy inference system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptive_neuro_fuzzy_inference_system">Adaptive neuro fuzzy inference system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or adaptive network-based fuzzy inference system (ANFIS) is a kind of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;that is based on Takagi&ndash;Sugeno fuzzy&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Inference system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_system">inference system</a>. The technique was developed in the early 1990s.&nbsp;Since it integrates both neural networks and&nbsp;<a title="Fuzzy logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_logic">fuzzy logic</a>&nbsp;principles, it has potential to capture the benefits of both in a single&nbsp;<a class="extiw" title="wikt:framework" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/framework">framework</a>. Its inference system corresponds to a set of fuzzy&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Conditional (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conditional_(programming)">IF&ndash;THEN rules</a>&nbsp;that have learning capability to approximate nonlinear functions.&nbsp;Hence, ANFIS is considered to be a universal estimator.&nbsp;For using the ANFIS in a more efficient and optimal way, one can use the best parameters obtained by genetic algorithm.</li>
<li><a title="Admissible heuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Admissible_heuristic">Admissible heuristic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, specifically in&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;related to&nbsp;<a title="Pathfinding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pathfinding">pathfinding</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Heuristic function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heuristic_function">heuristic function</a>&nbsp;is said to be admissible if it never overestimates the cost of reaching the goal, i.e. the cost it estimates to reach the goal is not higher than the lowest possible cost from the current point in the path.</li>
<li><a title="Affective computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affective_computing">Affective computing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (sometimes called artificial emotional intelligence, or emotion AI)&nbsp;is the study and development of systems and devices that can recognize, interpret, process, and simulate human&nbsp;<a title="Affect (psychology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affect_(psychology)">affects</a>. It is an interdisciplinary field spanning&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Psychology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">psychology</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science">cognitive science</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Agent architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_architecture">Agent architecture</a>&nbsp;&ndash; in&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Blueprint" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blueprint">blueprint</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Software agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_agent">software agents</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_control">intelligent control</a>&nbsp;systems, depicting the arrangement of components. The architectures implemented by&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>&nbsp;are referred to as&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_architecture">cognitive architectures</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="AI accelerator (computer hardware)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_accelerator_(computer_hardware)">AI accelerator</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a class of&nbsp;<a title="Microprocessor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microprocessor">microprocessor</a><span style="font-size: xx-small;">&nbsp;</span>or computer system designed as&nbsp;<a title="Hardware acceleration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardware_acceleration">hardware acceleration</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;applications, especially&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Machine vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_vision">machine vision</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="AI-complete" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI-complete">AI-complete</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In the field of artificial intelligence, the most difficult problems are informally known as AI-complete or AI-hard, implying that the difficulty of these computational problems is equivalent to that of solving the central artificial intelligence problem&mdash;making computers as intelligent as people, or&nbsp;<a title="Artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence">strong AI</a>. To call a problem AI-complete reflects an attitude that it would not be solved by a simple specific algorithm.</li>
<li><a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">Algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an unambiguous specification of how to solve a class of problems. Algorithms can perform calculation, data processing and automated reasoning tasks.</li>
<li><a title="Algorithmic efficiency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_efficiency">Algorithmic efficiency</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a property of an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;which relates to the number of&nbsp;<a title="Computational resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_resource">computational resources</a>&nbsp;used by the algorithm. An algorithm must be&nbsp;<a title="Analysis of algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analysis_of_algorithms">analyzed</a>&nbsp;to determine its resource usage, and the efficiency of an algorithm can be measured based on usage of different resources. Algorithmic efficiency can be thought of as analogous to engineering&nbsp;<a title="Productivity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Productivity">productivity</a>&nbsp;for a repeating or continuous process.</li>
<li><a title="Algorithmic probability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_probability">Algorithmic probability</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Algorithmic information theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_information_theory">algorithmic information theory</a>, algorithmic probability, also known as Solomonoff probability, is a mathematical method of assigning a prior&nbsp;<a title="Probability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability">probability</a>&nbsp;to a given observation. It was invented by&nbsp;<a title="Ray Solomonoff" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Solomonoff">Ray Solomonoff</a>&nbsp;in the 1960s.</li>
<li><a title="AlphaGo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaGo">AlphaGo</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;that plays the&nbsp;<a title="Board game" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Board_game">board game</a>&nbsp;<a title="Go (game)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go_(game)">Go</a>.&nbsp;It was developed by&nbsp;<a title="Alphabet Inc." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphabet_Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a>'s&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Google DeepMind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_DeepMind">Google DeepMind</a>&nbsp;in London. AlphaGo has several versions including&nbsp;<a title="AlphaGo Zero" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaGo_Zero">AlphaGo Zero</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="AlphaGo Master" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaGo_Master">AlphaGo Master</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="AlphaGo Lee" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaGo_Lee">AlphaGo Lee</a>, etc. In October 2015, AlphaGo became the first&nbsp;<a title="Computer Go" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_Go">computer Go</a>&nbsp;program to beat a human&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Professional Go player" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_Go_player">professional Go player</a>&nbsp;without&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Go handicaps" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go_handicaps">handicaps</a>&nbsp;on a full-sized 19&times;19 board.</li>
<li><a title="Ambient intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ambient_intelligence">Ambient intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (AmI) refers to electronic environments that are sensitive and responsive to the presence of people.</li>
<li><a title="Analysis of algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analysis_of_algorithms">Analysis of algorithms</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the determination of the&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity">computational complexity</a>&nbsp;of algorithms, that is the amount of time, storage and/or other resources necessary to&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">execute them</a>. Usually, this involves determining a&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>&nbsp;that relates the length of an algorithm's input to the number of steps it takes (its&nbsp;<a title="Time complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_complexity">time complexity</a>) or the number of storage locations it uses (its&nbsp;<a title="Space complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_complexity">space complexity</a>).</li>
<li><a title="Analytics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytics">Analytics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; the discovery, interpretation, and communication of meaningful patterns in data.</li>
<li><a title="Answer set programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Answer_set_programming">Answer set programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (ASP) is a form of&nbsp;<a title="Declarative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declarative_programming">declarative programming</a>&nbsp;oriented towards difficult (primarily&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="NP-hard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NP-hard">NP-hard</a>)&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search problems</a>. It is based on the&nbsp;<a title="Stable model semantics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stable_model_semantics">stable model</a>&nbsp;(answer set) semantics of&nbsp;<a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">logic programming</a>. In ASP, search problems are reduced to computing stable models, and&nbsp;<em>answer set solvers</em>&mdash;programs for generating stable models&mdash;are used to perform search.</li>
<li><a title="Anytime algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anytime_algorithm">Anytime algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; an algorithm that can return a valid solution to a problem even if it is interrupted before it ends.</li>
<li><a title="Application programming interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface">Application programming interface</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (API) is a set of subroutine definitions,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Communication protocols" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_protocols">communication protocols</a>, and tools for building software. In general terms, it is a set of clearly defined methods of communication among various components. A good API makes it easier to develop a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;by providing all the building blocks, which are then put together by the&nbsp;<a title="Programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmer">programmer</a>. An API may be for a web-based system,&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating system</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Database system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_system">database system</a>, computer hardware, or&nbsp;<a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">software library</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Approximate string matching" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximate_string_matching">Approximate string matching</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (often colloquially referred to as fuzzy string searching) is the technique of finding&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="String (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/String_(computing)">strings</a>&nbsp;that match a&nbsp;<a title="Pattern" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern">pattern</a>&nbsp;approximately (rather than exactly). The problem of approximate string matching is typically divided into two sub-problems: finding approximate&nbsp;<a title="Substring" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substring">substring</a>&nbsp;matches inside a given string and finding dictionary strings that match the pattern approximately.</li>
<li><a title="Approximation error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximation_error">Approximation error</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The approximation error in some data is the discrepancy between an exact value and some approximation to it.</li>
<li><a title="Argumentation framework" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argumentation_framework">Argumentation framework</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or argumentation system, is a way to deal with contentious information and draw conclusions from it. In an abstract argumentation framework,&nbsp;entry-level information is a set of abstract arguments that, for instance, represent data or a proposition. Conflicts between arguments are represented by a&nbsp;<a title="Binary relation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_relation">binary relation</a>&nbsp;on the set of arguments. In concrete terms, you represent an argumentation framework with a&nbsp;<a title="Directed graph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directed_graph">directed graph</a>&nbsp;such that the nodes are the arguments, and the arrows represent the attack relation. There exist some extensions of the Dung's framework, like the logic-based argumentation frameworks&nbsp;or the value-based argumentation frameworks.</li>
<li><a title="Artificial immune system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_immune_system">Artificial immune system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Artificial immune systems (AIS) are a class of computationally intelligent,&nbsp;<a title="Rule-based machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule-based_machine_learning">rule-based machine learning</a>&nbsp;systems inspired by the principles and processes of the vertebrate&nbsp;<a title="Immune system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immune_system">immune system</a>. The algorithms are typically modeled after the immune system's characteristics of&nbsp;<a title="Learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Learning">learning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory">memory</a>&nbsp;for use in&nbsp;<a title="Problem solving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problem_solving">problem-solving</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (AI), sometimes called machine intelligence, is&nbsp;<a title="Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence">intelligence</a>&nbsp;demonstrated by&nbsp;<a title="Machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine">machines</a>, in contrast to the natural intelligence displayed by humans and other animals. In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;AI research is defined as the study of "<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>": any device that perceives its environment and takes actions that maximize its chance of successfully achieving its goals.&nbsp;Colloquially, the term "artificial intelligence" is applied when a machine mimics "cognitive" functions that humans associate with other&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_mind">human minds</a>, such as "learning" and "problem solving".</li>
<li><a title="AIML" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIML">Artificial Intelligence Markup Language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="XML" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XML">XML</a>&nbsp;dialect for creating&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural language</a>&nbsp;software agents.</li>
<li><a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">Artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (ANN) or&nbsp;<a title="Connectionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Connectionism">connectionist</a>&nbsp;systems are computing systems vaguely inspired by the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_neural_network">biological neural networks</a>&nbsp;that constitute animal&nbsp;<a title="Brain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain">brains</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Association for the Advancement of Artificial Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Artificial_Intelligence">Association for the Advancement of Artificial Intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (AAAI) is an international, nonprofit, scientific society devoted to promote research in, and responsible use of,&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>. AAAI also aims to increase public understanding of artificial intelligence (AI), improve the teaching and training of AI practitioners, and provide guidance for research planners and funders concerning the importance and potential of current AI developments and future directions.</li>
<li><a title="Asymptotic computational complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asymptotic_computational_complexity">Asymptotic computational complexity</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">computational complexity theory</a>, asymptotic computational complexity is the usage of&nbsp;<a title="Asymptotic analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asymptotic_analysis">asymptotic analysis</a>&nbsp;for the estimation of computational complexity of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computational problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_problem">computational problems</a>, commonly associated with the usage of the&nbsp;<a title="Big O notation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation">big O notation</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Attributional calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attributional_calculus">Attributional calculus</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a logic and representation system defined by&nbsp;<a title="Ryszard S. Michalski" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryszard_S._Michalski">Ryszard S. Michalski</a>. It combines elements of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Predicate logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predicate_logic">predicate logic</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Propositional calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_calculus">propositional calculus</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-valued logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-valued_logic">multi-valued logic</a>. Attributional calculus provides a formal language for&nbsp;<em>natural induction</em>, an inductive learning process whose results are in forms natural to people.</li>
<li><a title="Augmented reality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augmented_reality">Augmented reality</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (AR) is an interactive experience of a real-world environment where the objects that reside in the real-world are "augmented" by computer-generated perceptual information, sometimes across multiple sensory modalities, including&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Visual" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual">visual</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Hearing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hearing">auditory</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Haptic perception" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptic_perception">haptic</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Somatosensory system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somatosensory_system">somatosensory</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Olfactory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olfactory">olfactory</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Automata theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automata_theory">Automata theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of&nbsp;<a title="Abstract machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_machine">abstract machines</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Automaton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automaton">automata</a>, as well as the&nbsp;<a title="Computational problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_problem">computational problems</a>&nbsp;that can be solved using them. It is a theory in&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Discrete mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_mathematics">discrete mathematics</a>&nbsp;(a subject of study in both&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>).</li>
<li><a title="Automated planning and scheduling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning_and_scheduling">Automated planning and scheduling</a>&nbsp;&ndash; sometimes denoted as simply AI Planning,&nbsp;is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;that concerns the realization of&nbsp;<a title="Strategy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategy">strategies</a>&nbsp;or action sequences, typically for execution by&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Autonomous robot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_robot">autonomous robots</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Unmanned vehicle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unmanned_vehicle">unmanned vehicles</a>. Unlike classical&nbsp;<a title="Control system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_system">control</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">classification</a>&nbsp;problems, the solutions are complex and must be discovered and optimized in multidimensional space. Planning is also related to&nbsp;<a title="Decision theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_theory">decision theory</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">Automated reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an area of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">mathematical logic</a>&nbsp;dedicated to understanding different aspects of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning">reasoning</a>. The study of automated reasoning helps produce&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer programs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programs">computer programs</a>&nbsp;that allow computers to reason completely, or nearly completely, automatically. Although automated reasoning is considered a sub-field of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, it also has connections with&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>, and even&nbsp;<a title="Philosophy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">philosophy</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Autonomic computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomic_computing">Autonomic computing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as AC) refers to the&nbsp;<a title="Self-management (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-management_(computer_science)">self-managing</a>&nbsp;characteristics of&nbsp;<a title="Distributed computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_computing">distributed computing</a>&nbsp;resources, adapting to unpredictable changes while hiding intrinsic complexity to operators and users. Initiated by&nbsp;<a title="IBM" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM">IBM</a>&nbsp;in 2001, this initiative ultimately aimed to develop computer systems capable of self-management, to overcome the rapidly growing complexity of computing&nbsp;<a title="Systems management" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_management">systems management</a>, and to reduce the barrier that complexity poses to further growth.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous car" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_car">Autonomous car</a>&nbsp;&ndash; A self-driving car, also known as a robot car, autonomous car, auto, or driverless car,&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Vehicular automation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vehicular_automation">vehicle</a>&nbsp;that is capable of sensing its environment and moving with little or no&nbsp;<a title="User interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_interface">human input</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Autonomous robot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_robot">Autonomous robot</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Robot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot">robot</a>&nbsp;that performs&nbsp;<a title="Behavior-based robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavior-based_robotics">behaviors</a>&nbsp;or tasks with a high degree of&nbsp;<a title="Autonomy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomy">autonomy</a>. Autonomous robotics is usually considered to be a subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">robotics</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Information engineering (field)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_engineering_(field)">information engineering</a>.</li>
</ul>


<h2><span id="B" class="mw-headline">B</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Backpropagation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backpropagation">Backpropagation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a method used in&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;to calculate a&nbsp;<a title="Gradient" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient">gradient</a>&nbsp;that is needed in the calculation of the&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network#Components_of_an_artificial_neural_network">weights</a>&nbsp;to be used in the network.&nbsp;Backpropagation is shorthand for "the backward propagation of errors," since an error is computed at the output and distributed backwards throughout the network's layers. It is commonly used to train&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Deep neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_neural_network">deep neural networks</a>,&nbsp;a term referring to neural networks with more than one hidden layer.</li>
<li><a title="Backpropagation through time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backpropagation_through_time">Backpropagation through time</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (BPTT) is a&nbsp;<a title="Gradient" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient">gradient</a>-based technique for training certain types of&nbsp;<a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network">recurrent neural networks</a>. It can be used to train&nbsp;<a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network#Elman_networks_and_Jordan_networks">Elman networks</a>. The algorithm was independently derived by numerous researchers.</li>
<li><a title="Backward chaining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backward_chaining">Backward chaining</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (or backward reasoning) is an&nbsp;<a title="Inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference">inference</a>&nbsp;method described colloquially as working backward from the goal. It is used in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Automated theorem prover" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_theorem_prover">automated theorem provers</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engines</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Proof assistant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proof_assistant">proof assistants</a>, and other&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;applications.</li>
<li><a title="Bag-of-words model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bag-of-words_model">Bag-of-words model</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a simplifying representation used in&nbsp;<a title="Natural language processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing">natural language processing</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Information retrieval" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_retrieval">information retrieval</a>&nbsp;(IR). In this model, a text (such as a sentence or a document) is represented as the&nbsp;<a title="Multiset" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiset">bag (multiset)</a>&nbsp;of its words, disregarding grammar and even word order but keeping&nbsp;<a title="Multiplicity (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiplicity_(mathematics)">multiplicity</a>. The bag-of-words model has also been&nbsp;<a title="Bag-of-words model in computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bag-of-words_model_in_computer_vision">used for computer vision</a>.&nbsp;The bag-of-words model is commonly used in methods of&nbsp;<a title="Document classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Document_classification">document classification</a>&nbsp;where the (frequency of) occurrence of each word is used as a&nbsp;<a title="Feature (machine learning)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_(machine_learning)">feature</a>&nbsp;for training a&nbsp;<a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">classifier</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Bag-of-words model in computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bag-of-words_model_in_computer_vision">Bag-of-words model in computer vision</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In computer vision, the bag-of-words model (BoW model) can be applied to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Image classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_classification">image classification</a>, by treating&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Image feature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_feature">image features</a>&nbsp;as words. In document classification, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bag of words" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bag_of_words">bag of words</a>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sparse vector" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sparse_vector">sparse vector</a>&nbsp;of occurrence counts of words; that is, a sparse&nbsp;<a title="Histogram" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Histogram">histogram</a>&nbsp;over the vocabulary. In&nbsp;<a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">computer vision</a>, a&nbsp;<em>bag of visual words</em>&nbsp;is a vector of occurrence counts of a vocabulary of local image features.</li>
<li><a title="Batch normalization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batch_normalization">Batch normalization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a technique for improving the performance and stability of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>. It is a technique to provide any layer in a neural network with inputs that are zero mean/unit variance.&nbsp;Batch normalization was introduced in a 2015 paper.&nbsp;It is used to normalize the input layer by adjusting and scaling the activations.</li>
<li><a title="Bayesian programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayesian_programming">Bayesian programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a formalism and a methodology for having a technique to specify&nbsp;<a title="Probability distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_distribution">probabilistic models</a>&nbsp;and solve problems when less than the necessary information is available.</li>
<li><a title="Bees algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bees_algorithm">Bees algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a population-based&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search algorithm</a>&nbsp;which was developed by Pham, Ghanbarzadeh and et al. in 2005.&nbsp;It mimics the food foraging behaviour of honey bee colonies. In its basic version the algorithm performs a kind of neighbourhood search combined with global search, and can be used for both&nbsp;<a title="Combinatorial optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combinatorial_optimization">combinatorial optimization</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Continuous optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuous_optimization">continuous optimization</a>. The only condition for the application of the bees algorithm is that some measure of distance between the solutions is defined. The effectiveness and specific abilities of the bees algorithm have been proven in a number of studies.<sup id="cite_ref-Nasrinpour_&amp;_Massah_&amp;_Teshnehlab_2017_55-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><a title="Behavior informatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavior_informatics">Behavior informatics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (BI) is the informatics of behaviors so as to obtain behavior intelligence and behavior insights.</li>
<li><a title="Behavior tree (artificial intelligence, robotics and control)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavior_tree_(artificial_intelligence,_robotics_and_control)">Behavior tree</a>&nbsp;&ndash; A Behavior Tree (BT) is a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical model</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Automated planning and scheduling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning_and_scheduling">plan</a>&nbsp;execution used in&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">robotics</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Control systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_systems">control systems</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial intelligence (video games)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence_(video_games)">video games</a>. They describe switchings between a finite set of tasks in a modular fashion. Their strength comes from their ability to create very complex tasks composed of simple tasks, without worrying how the simple tasks are implemented. BTs present some similarities to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="State machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_machine">hierarchical state machines</a>&nbsp;with the key difference that the main building block of a behavior is a task rather than a state. Its ease of human understanding make BTs less error-prone and very popular in the game developer community. BTs have shown to generalize several other control architectures.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Belief-desire-intention software model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belief-desire-intention_software_model">Belief-desire-intention software model</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (BDI), is a software model developed for programming&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>. Superficially characterized by the implementation of an agent's&nbsp;<em>beliefs</em>,&nbsp;<em>desires</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>intentions</em>, it actually uses these concepts to solve a particular problem in agent programming. In essence, it provides a mechanism for separating the activity of selecting a plan (from a plan library or an external planner application) from the execution of currently active plans. Consequently, BDI agents are able to balance the time spent on deliberating about plans (choosing what to do) and executing those plans (doing it). A third activity, creating the plans in the first place (planning), is not within the scope of the model, and is left to the system designer and programmer.</li>
<li><a title="Bias&ndash;variance tradeoff" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bias%E2%80%93variance_tradeoff">Bias&ndash;variance tradeoff</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, the bias&ndash;variance tradeoff is the property of a set of predictive models whereby models with a lower&nbsp;<a title="Bias of an estimator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bias_of_an_estimator">bias</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Statistical parameter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_parameter">parameter</a>&nbsp;<a title="Estimation theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estimation_theory">estimation</a>&nbsp;have a higher&nbsp;<a title="Variance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variance">variance</a>&nbsp;of the parameter estimates across&nbsp;<a title="Sample (statistics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sample_(statistics)">samples</a>, and vice versa.</li>
<li><a title="Big data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_data">Big data</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a term used to refer to&nbsp;<a title="Data set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_set">data sets</a>&nbsp;that are too large or complex for traditional&nbsp;<a title="Data processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_processing">data-processing</a>&nbsp;<a title="Application software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_software">application software</a>&nbsp;to adequately deal with. Data with many cases (rows) offer greater&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical power" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_power">statistical power</a>, while data with higher complexity (more attributes or columns) may lead to a higher&nbsp;<a title="False discovery rate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_discovery_rate">false discovery rate</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Big O notation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation">Big O notation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a mathematical notation that describes the&nbsp;<a title="Asymptotic analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asymptotic_analysis">limiting behavior</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>&nbsp;when the&nbsp;<a title="Argument of a function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argument_of_a_function">argument</a>&nbsp;tends towards a particular value or infinity. It is a member of a family of notations invented by&nbsp;<a title="Paul Gustav Heinrich Bachmann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Gustav_Heinrich_Bachmann">Paul Bachmann</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Edmund Landau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Landau">Edmund Landau</a>,&nbsp;and others, collectively called Bachmann&ndash;Landau notation or asymptotic notation.</li>
<li><a title="Binary tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_tree">Binary tree</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Tree structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_structure">tree</a>&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;in which each node has at most two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Child node" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_node">children</a>, which are referred to as the&nbsp;<em><span id="left_child">left child</span></em>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<em><span id="right_child">right child</span></em>. A&nbsp;<a title="Recursive definition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recursive_definition">recursive definition</a>&nbsp;using just&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">set theory</a>&nbsp;notions is that a (non-empty) binary tree is a&nbsp;<a title="Tuple" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuple">tuple</a>&nbsp;(<em>L</em>,&nbsp;<em>S</em>,&nbsp;<em>R</em>), where&nbsp;<em>L</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>R</em>&nbsp;are binary trees or the&nbsp;<a title="Empty set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empty_set">empty set</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>S</em>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Singleton set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singleton_set">singleton set</a>.&nbsp;Some authors allow the binary tree to be the empty set as well.</li>
<li><a title="Blackboard system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blackboard_system">Blackboard system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;approach based on the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Blackboard design pattern" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blackboard_design_pattern">blackboard architectural model</a>,&nbsp;where a common knowledge base, the "blackboard", is iteratively updated by a diverse group of specialist knowledge sources, starting with a problem specification and ending with a solution. Each knowledge source updates the blackboard with a partial solution when its internal constraints match the blackboard state. In this way, the specialists work together to solve the problem.</li>
<li><a title="Boltzmann machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boltzmann_machine">Boltzmann machine</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also called stochastic Hopfield network with hidden units) is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_neural_network">stochastic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network">recurrent neural network</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Markov random field" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_random_field">Markov random field</a>.&nbsp;Boltzmann machines can be seen as the&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_process">stochastic</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Generative model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_model">generative</a>&nbsp;counterpart of&nbsp;<a title="Hopfield network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hopfield_network">Hopfield networks</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Boolean satisfiability problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_satisfiability_problem">Boolean satisfiability problem</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (sometimes called propositional satisfiability problem and abbreviated SATISFIABILITY or SAT) is the problem of determining if there exists an&nbsp;<a title="Interpretation (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpretation_(logic)">interpretation</a>&nbsp;that&nbsp;<a title="Satisfiability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satisfiability">satisfies</a>&nbsp;a given&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Boolean logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_logic">Boolean</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formula (mathematical logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formula_(mathematical_logic)">formula</a>. In other words, it asks whether the variables of a given Boolean formula can be consistently replaced by the values TRUE or FALSE in such a way that the formula&nbsp;<a title="Validity (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Validity_(logic)">evaluates to TRUE</a>. If this is the case, the formula is called&nbsp;<em>satisfiable</em>. On the other hand, if no such assignment exists, the function expressed by the formula is&nbsp;<a title="Contradiction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contradiction#Contradiction_in_formal_logic">FALSE</a>&nbsp;for all possible variable assignments and the formula is&nbsp;<em>unsatisfiable</em>. For example, the formula "<em>a</em>&nbsp;AND NOT&nbsp;<em>b</em>" is satisfiable because one can find the values&nbsp;<em>a</em>&nbsp;=&nbsp;TRUE and&nbsp;<em>b</em>&nbsp;=&nbsp;FALSE, which make (<em>a</em>&nbsp;AND NOT&nbsp;<em>b</em>)&nbsp;=&nbsp;TRUE. In contrast, "<em>a</em>&nbsp;AND NOT&nbsp;<em>a</em>" is unsatisfiable.</li>
<li><a title="Brain technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain_technology">Brain technology</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or self-learning know-how systems, defines a technology that employs latest findings in&nbsp;<a title="Neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>. The term was first introduced by the Artificial Intelligence Laboratory in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich, Switzerland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zurich,_Switzerland">Zurich, Switzerland</a>, in the context of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="ROBOY" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ROBOY">ROBOY</a>&nbsp;project.&nbsp;Brain Technology can be employed in robots,&nbsp;<a title="Starmind International" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Starmind_International">know-how management systems</a>&nbsp;and any other application with self-learning capabilities. In particular, Brain Technology applications allow the visualization of the underlying learning architecture often coined as "know-how maps".</li>
<li><a title="Branching factor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branching_factor">Branching factor</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Tree data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_data_structure">tree data structures</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Game theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory">game theory</a>, the branching factor is the number of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Child node" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_node">children</a>&nbsp;at each&nbsp;<a title="Node (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(computer_science)">node</a>, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Outdegree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outdegree">outdegree</a>. If this value is not uniform, an&nbsp;<em>average branching factor</em>&nbsp;can be calculated.</li>
<li><a title="Brute-force search" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brute-force_search">Brute-force search</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or exhaustive search, also known as generate and test, is a very general&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Problem-solving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problem-solving">problem-solving</a>&nbsp;technique and&nbsp;<a title="Algorithmic paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_paradigm">algorithmic paradigm</a>&nbsp;that consists of systematically enumerating all possible candidates for the solution and checking whether each candidate satisfies the problem's statement.</li>
</ul>


<h2><span id="C" class="mw-headline">C</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Capsule neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capsule_neural_network">Capsule neural network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; A Capsule Neural Network (CapsNet) is a machine learning system that is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;(ANN) that can be used to better model hierarchical relationships. The approach is an attempt to more closely mimic biological neural organization.</li>
<li><a title="Case-based reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Case-based_reasoning">Case-based reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (CBR), broadly construed, is the process of solving new problems based on the solutions of similar past problems.</li>
<li><a title="Chatbot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chatbot">Chatbot</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as a smartbots, talkbot, chatterbot, Bot, IM bot, interactive agent, Conversational interface or Artificial Conversational Entity) is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;or an&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;which conducts a&nbsp;<a title="Conversation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conversation">conversation</a>&nbsp;via auditory or textual methods.</li>
<li><a title="Cloud robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_robotics">Cloud robotics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a field of&nbsp;<a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">robotics</a>&nbsp;that attempts to invoke cloud technologies such as&nbsp;<a title="Cloud computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_computing">cloud computing</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Cloud storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_storage">cloud storage</a>, and other&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Internet technologies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_technologies">Internet technologies</a>&nbsp;centred on the benefits of converged infrastructure and shared services for robotics. When connected to the cloud, robots can benefit from the powerful computation, storage, and communication resources of modern&nbsp;<a title="Data center" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_center">data center</a>&nbsp;in the cloud, which can process and share information from various robots or agent (other machines, smart objects, humans, etc.). Humans can also delegate tasks to robots remotely through&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Network (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_(computing)">networks</a>. Cloud computing technologies enable robot systems to be endowed with powerful capability whilst reducing costs through cloud technologies. Thus, it is possible to build lightweight, low cost, smarter robots have intelligent "brain" in the cloud. The "brain" consists of&nbsp;<a title="Data center" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_center">data center</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_base">knowledge base</a>, task planners,&nbsp;<a title="Deep learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_learning">deep learning</a>, information processing, environment models, communication support, etc.</li>
<li><a title="Cluster analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cluster_analysis">Cluster analysis</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or clustering is the task of grouping a set of objects in such a way that objects in the same group (called a cluster) are more similar (in some sense) to each other than to those in other groups (clusters). It is a main task of exploratory&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data mining</a>, and a common technique for&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistical</a>&nbsp;<a title="Data analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_analysis">data analysis</a>, used in many fields, including&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pattern recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_recognition">pattern recognition</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Image analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_analysis">image analysis</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information retrieval" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_retrieval">information retrieval</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Bioinformatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioinformatics">bioinformatics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Data compression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_compression">data compression</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computer graphics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_graphics">computer graphics</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Cobweb (clustering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cobweb_(clustering)">Cobweb</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an incremental system for hierarchical&nbsp;<a title="Conceptual clustering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conceptual_clustering">conceptual clustering</a>. COBWEB was invented by Professor&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Douglas H. Fisher (Computer Science) (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Douglas_H._Fisher_(Computer_Science)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Douglas H. Fisher</a>, currently at Vanderbilt University.&nbsp;COBWEB incrementally organizes observations into a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Classification tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classification_tree">classification tree</a>. Each node in a classification tree represents a class (concept) and is labeled by a probabilistic concept that summarizes the attribute-value distributions of objects classified under the node. This classification tree can be used to predict missing attributes or the class of a new object.</li>
<li><a title="Cognitive architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_architecture">Cognitive architecture</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Creative Technologies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_Creative_Technologies">Institute of Creative Technologies</a>&nbsp;defines cognitive architecture as: "hypothesis about the fixed structures that provide a mind, whether in natural or artificial systems, and how they work together &ndash; in conjunction with knowledge and skills embodied within the architecture &ndash; to yield intelligent behavior in a diversity of complex environments."</li>
<li><a title="Cognitive computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_computing">Cognitive computing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In general, the term cognitive computing has been used to refer to new hardware and/or software that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Neuromorphic computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuromorphic_computing">mimics the functioning</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Human brain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain">human brain</a>&nbsp;and helps to improve human decision-making.&nbsp;In this sense, CC is a new type of computing with the goal of more accurate models of how the human brain/<a title="Mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind">mind</a>&nbsp;senses,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning">reasons</a>, and responds to stimulus.</li>
<li><a title="Cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science">Cognitive science</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the interdisciplinary,&nbsp;<a title="Science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science">scientific</a>&nbsp;study of the&nbsp;<a title="Mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind">mind</a>&nbsp;and its processes.</li>
<li><a title="Combinatorial optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combinatorial_optimization">Combinatorial optimization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Operations Research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operations_Research">Operations Research</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Applied mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applied_mathematics">applied mathematics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>, combinatorial optimization is a topic that consists of finding an optimal object from a&nbsp;<a title="Finite set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finite_set">finite set</a>&nbsp;of objects.</li>
<li><a title="Committee machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_machine">Committee machine</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;using a&nbsp;<a title="Divide and rule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divide_and_rule">divide and conquer</a>&nbsp;strategy in which the responses of multiple neural networks (experts) are combined into a single response.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_artificial_intelligence#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>&nbsp;The combined response of the committee machine is supposed to be superior to those of its constituent experts. Compare with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ensembles of classifiers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ensembles_of_classifiers">ensembles of classifiers</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Commonsense knowledge (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_knowledge_(artificial_intelligence)">Commonsense knowledge</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;research, commonsense knowledge consists of facts about the everyday world, such as "Lemons are sour", that all humans are expected to know. The first AI program to address common sense knowledge was&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Advice Taker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advice_Taker">Advice Taker</a>&nbsp;in 1959 by John McCarthy.</li>
<li><a title="Commonsense reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_reasoning">Commonsense reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is one of the branches of artificial intelligence that is concerned with simulating the human ability to make presumptions about the type and essence of ordinary situations they encounter every day.</li>
<li><a title="Computational chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_chemistry">Computational chemistry</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry">chemistry</a>&nbsp;that uses&nbsp;<a title="Computer simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_simulation">computer simulation</a>&nbsp;to assist in solving chemical problems.</li>
<li><a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">Computational complexity theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; focuses on classifying computational problems according to their inherent difficulty, and relating these classes to each other. A computational problem is a task solved by a computer. A computation problem is solvable by mechanical application of mathematical steps, such as an algorithm.</li>
<li><a title="Computational creativity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_creativity">Computational creativity</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as artificial creativity, mechanical creativity, creative computing or creative computation) is a multidisciplinary endeavour that includes the fields of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive psychology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_psychology">cognitive psychology</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Philosophy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">philosophy</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="The arts" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_arts">the arts</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computational cybernetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_cybernetics">Computational cybernetics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the integration of&nbsp;<a title="Cybernetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cybernetics">cybernetics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computational intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_intelligence">computational intelligence</a>&nbsp;techniques.</li>
<li><a title="Computational humor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_humor">Computational humor</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Computational linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_linguistics">computational linguistics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;which uses&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computers</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Humor research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humor_research">humor research</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computational intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_intelligence">Computational intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (CI), usually refers to the ability of a&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;to learn a specific task from data or experimental observation.</li>
<li><a title="Computational learning theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_learning_theory">Computational learning theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, computational learning theory (or just learning theory) is a subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;devoted to studying the design and analysis of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;algorithms.</li>
<li><a title="Computational linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_linguistics">Computational linguistics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interdisciplinary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinary">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;field concerned with the statistical or rule-based modeling of&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural language</a>&nbsp;from a computational perspective, as well as the study of appropriate computational approaches to linguistic questions.</li>
<li><a title="Computational mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_mathematics">Computational mathematics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; the mathematical research in areas of science where&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computing</a>&nbsp;plays an essential role.</li>
<li><a title="Computational neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_neuroscience">Computational neuroscience</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as theoretical neuroscience or mathematical neuroscience) is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>&nbsp;which employs mathematical models, theoretical analysis and abstractions of the brain to understand the principles that govern the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Developmental neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developmental_neuroscience">development</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Neuroanatomy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroanatomy">structure</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Neurophysiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurophysiology">physiology</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience">cognitive abilities</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Nervous system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nervous_system">nervous system</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computational number theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_number_theory">Computational number theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; also known as&nbsp;<em>algorithmic number theory</em>, it is the study of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;for performing&nbsp;<a title="Number theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_theory">number theoretic</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computations">computations</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computational problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_problem">Computational problem</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>, a computational problem is a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical object" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_object">mathematical object</a>&nbsp;representing a collection of questions that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computers">computers</a>&nbsp;might be able to solve.</li>
<li><a title="Computational statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_statistics">Computational statistics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or statistical computing, is the interface between&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computer-automated design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer-automated_design">Computer-automated design</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Design Automation usually refers to&nbsp;<a title="Electronic design automation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_design_automation">electronic design automation</a>, or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Design Automation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design_Automation">Design Automation</a>&nbsp;which is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Product Configurator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_Configurator">Product Configurator</a>. Extending&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer-Aided Design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer-Aided_Design">Computer-Aided Design</a>&nbsp;(CAD), automated design and Computer-Automated Design (CAutoD)&nbsp;are more concerned with a broader range of applications, such as&nbsp;<a title="Automotive engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_engineering">automotive engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Civil engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_engineering">civil engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Composite material" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Composite_material">composite material</a>&nbsp;design,&nbsp;<a title="Control engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_engineering">control engineering</a>,&nbsp;dynamic&nbsp;<a title="System identification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_identification">system identification</a>&nbsp;and optimization,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Financial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial">financial</a>&nbsp;systems, industrial equipment,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mechatronic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechatronic">mechatronic</a>&nbsp;systems,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Steel construction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steel_construction">steel construction</a>,&nbsp;structural&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Optimization (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_(mathematics)">optimisation</a>, and the invention of novel systems. More recently, traditional CAD simulation is seen to be transformed to CAutoD by biologically-inspired&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>,&nbsp;including heuristic&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search techniques</a>&nbsp;such as&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation">evolutionary computation</a>,&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Swarm intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swarm_intelligence">swarm intelligence</a>&nbsp;algorithms.</li>
<li><a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">Computer science</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the theory, experimentation, and engineering that form the basis for the design and use of&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computers</a>. It involves the study of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;that process, store, and communicate&nbsp;<a title="Digital data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_data">digital</a>&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>. A&nbsp;<a title="Computer scientist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_scientist">computer scientist</a>&nbsp;specializes in the theory of computation and the design of computational systems.</li>
<li><a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">Computer vision</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Interdisciplinarity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinary scientific field</a>&nbsp;that deals with how computers can be made to gain high-level understanding from&nbsp;<a title="Digital image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_image">digital images</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Video" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video">videos</a>. From the perspective of&nbsp;<a title="Engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering">engineering</a>, it seeks to automate tasks that the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human visual system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_visual_system">human visual system</a>&nbsp;can do.</li>
<li><a title="Concept drift" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concept_drift">Concept drift</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Predictive analytics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predictive_analytics">predictive analytics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, the concept drift means that the statistical properties of the target variable, which the model is trying to predict, change over time in unforeseen ways. This causes problems because the predictions become less accurate as time passes.</li>
<li><a title="Connectionism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Connectionism">Connectionism</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an approach in the fields of&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science">cognitive science</a>, that hopes to explain&nbsp;<a title="Mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind">mental</a>&nbsp;phenomena using&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_networks">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;(ANN).</li>
<li><a title="Consistent heuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consistent_heuristic">Consistent heuristic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In the study of&nbsp;<a title="Shortest path problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortest_path_problem">path-finding problems</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Heuristic function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heuristic_function">heuristic function</a>&nbsp;is said to be consistent, or monotone, if its estimate is always less than or equal to the estimated distance from any neighboring vertex to the goal, plus the cost of reaching that neighbor.</li>
<li><a title="Constrained conditional model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constrained_conditional_model">Constrained conditional model</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (CCM), is a&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;and inference framework that augments the learning of conditional (probabilistic or discriminative) models with declarative constraints.</li>
<li><a title="Constraint logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constraint_logic_programming">Constraint logic programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a form of&nbsp;<a title="Constraint programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constraint_programming">constraint programming</a>, in which&nbsp;<a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">logic programming</a>&nbsp;is extended to include concepts from&nbsp;<a title="Constraint satisfaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constraint_satisfaction">constraint satisfaction</a>. A constraint logic program is a logic program that contains constraints in the body of clauses. An example of a clause including a constraint is&nbsp;<code id="" class="mw-highlight" dir="ltr"><span class="nv">A</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">X</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="nv">Y</span><span class="p">)</span>&nbsp;<span class="p">:-</span>&nbsp;<span class="nv">X</span><span class="o">+</span><span class="nv">Y</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span>&nbsp;<span class="nv">B</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">X</span><span class="p">),</span>&nbsp;<span class="nv">C</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">Y</span><span class="p">)</span></code>.
