In this clause,&nbsp;<code id="" class="mw-highlight" dir="ltr"><span class="nv">X</span><span class="o">+</span><span class="nv">Y</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="mi">0</span></code>&nbsp;is a constraint;&nbsp;<code>A(X,Y)</code>,&nbsp;<code>B(X)</code>, and&nbsp;<code>C(Y)</code>&nbsp;are&nbsp;<a title="Literal (mathematical logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literal_(mathematical_logic)">literals</a>&nbsp;as in regular logic programming. This clause states one condition under which the statement&nbsp;<code>A(X,Y)</code>&nbsp;holds:&nbsp;<code>X+Y</code>&nbsp;is greater than zero and both&nbsp;<code>B(X)</code>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<code>C(Y)</code>&nbsp;are true.</li>
<li><a title="Constraint programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constraint_programming">Constraint programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;wherein&nbsp;<a title="Finitary relation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finitary_relation">relations</a>&nbsp;between&nbsp;<a title="Variable (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(mathematics)">variables</a>&nbsp;are stated in the form of&nbsp;<a title="Constraint (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constraint_(mathematics)">constraints</a>. Constraints differ from the common&nbsp;<a title="Language primitive" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_primitive">primitives</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Imperative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperative_programming">imperative programming</a>&nbsp;languages in that they do not specify a step or sequence of steps to execute, but rather the properties of a solution to be found.</li>
<li><a title="Constructed language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constructed_language">Constructed language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (sometimes called a conlang) is a&nbsp;<a title="Language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language">language</a>&nbsp;whose&nbsp;<a title="Phonology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phonology">phonology</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Grammar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammar">grammar</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Vocabulary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vocabulary">vocabulary</a>&nbsp;are, instead of having developed&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">naturally</a>, consciously devised. Constructed languages may also be referred to as artificial, planned or invented languages<span style="font-size: xx-small;">.</span></li>
<li><a title="Control theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_theory">Control theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; in&nbsp;<a title="Control engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_engineering">control systems engineering</a>&nbsp;is a subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;that deals with the control of continuously operating&nbsp;<a title="Dynamical system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamical_system">dynamical systems</a>&nbsp;in engineered processes and machines. The objective is to develop a control model for controlling such systems using a control action in an optimum manner without&nbsp;<em>delay or overshoot</em>&nbsp;and ensuring control&nbsp;<a title="Stability theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stability_theory">stability</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Convolutional neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convolutional_neural_network">Convolutional neural network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Deep learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_learning">deep learning</a>, a convolutional neural network (CNN, or ConvNet) is a class of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Deep neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_neural_network">deep neural networks</a>, most commonly applied to analyzing visual imagery. CNNs use a variation of&nbsp;<a title="Multilayer perceptron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multilayer_perceptron">multilayer perceptrons</a>&nbsp;designed to require minimal&nbsp;<a title="Data pre-processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_pre-processing">preprocessing</a>.&nbsp;They are also known as shift invariant or space invariant artificial neural networks (SIANN), based on their shared-weights architecture and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Translation invariance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translation_invariance">translation invariance</a>&nbsp;characteristics.</li>
<li><a title="Crossover (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossover_(genetic_algorithm)">Crossover</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Genetic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithm">genetic algorithms</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation">evolutionary computation</a>, crossover, also called recombination, is a&nbsp;<a title="Genetic operator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_operator">genetic operator</a>&nbsp;used to combine the&nbsp;<a title="Chromosome (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome_(genetic_algorithm)">genetic information</a>&nbsp;of two parents to generate new offspring. It is one way to&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic">stochastically</a>&nbsp;generate new&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Candidate solution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Candidate_solution">solutions</a>&nbsp;from an existing population, and analogous to the&nbsp;<a title="Chromosomal crossover" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosomal_crossover">crossover</a>&nbsp;that happens during&nbsp;<a title="Sexual reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_reproduction">sexual reproduction</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology">biology</a>. Solutions can also be generated by&nbsp;<a title="Cloning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloning">cloning</a>&nbsp;an existing solution, which is analogous to&nbsp;<a title="Asexual reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asexual_reproduction">asexual reproduction</a>. Newly generated solutions are typically&nbsp;<a title="Mutation (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation_(genetic_algorithm)">mutated</a>&nbsp;before being added to the population.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span id="D" class="mw-headline">D</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Darkforest" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darkforest">Darkforest</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer go" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_go">computer go</a>&nbsp;program developed by&nbsp;<a title="Facebook" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook">Facebook</a>, based on&nbsp;<a title="Deep learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_learning">deep learning</a>&nbsp;techniques using a&nbsp;<a title="Convolutional neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convolutional_neural_network">convolutional neural network</a>. Its updated version Darkfores2 combines the techniques of its predecessor with&nbsp;<a title="Monte Carlo tree search" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monte_Carlo_tree_search">Monte Carlo tree search</a>.&nbsp;The MCTS effectively takes tree search methods commonly seen in computer chess programs and randomizes them.&nbsp;With the update, the system is known as Darkfmcts3.</li>
<li><a title="Dartmouth workshop" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dartmouth_workshop">Dartmouth workshop</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The Dartmouth Summer Research Project on Artificial Intelligence was the name of a 1956 summer workshop now considered by many&nbsp;(though not all) to be the&nbsp;<a class="extiw" title="wikt:seminal" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/seminal">seminal</a>&nbsp;event for&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;as a field.</li>
<li><a title="Data fusion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_fusion">Data fusion</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process of integrating multiple data sources to produce more consistent, accurate, and useful information than that provided by any individual data source.</li>
<li><a title="Data integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_integration">Data integration</a>&nbsp;&ndash; involves combining&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>&nbsp;residing in different sources and providing users with a unified view of them.&nbsp;This process becomes significant in a variety of situations, which include both commercial (such as when two similar companies need to merge their&nbsp;<a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database">databases</a>) and scientific (combining research results from different&nbsp;<a title="Bioinformatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioinformatics">bioinformatics</a>&nbsp;repositories, for example) domains. Data integration appears with increasing frequency as the volume (that is,&nbsp;<a title="Big data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_data">big data</a>) and the need to share existing data&nbsp;<a title="Information explosion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_explosion">explodes</a>.&nbsp;It has become the focus of extensive theoretical work, and numerous open problems remain unsolved.</li>
<li><a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">Data mining</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process of discovering patterns in large data sets involving methods at the intersection of machine learning, statistics, and database systems.</li>
<li><a title="Data science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_science">Data science</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interdisciplinary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinary">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;field that uses scientific methods, processes, algorithms and systems to extract&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge">knowledge</a>&nbsp;and insights from&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>&nbsp;in various forms, both structured and unstructured,&nbsp;similar to&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data mining</a>. Data science is a "concept to unify statistics, data analysis, machine learning and their related methods" in order to "understand and analyze actual phenomena" with data.&nbsp;It employs techniques and theories drawn from many fields within the context of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_science">information science</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Data set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_set">Data set</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (or dataset) is a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>. Most commonly a data set corresponds to the contents of a single&nbsp;<a title="Table (database)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Table_(database)">database table</a>, or a single statistical&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Data matrix (multivariate statistics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_matrix_(multivariate_statistics)">data matrix</a>, where every&nbsp;<a title="Column (database)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Column_(database)">column</a>&nbsp;of the table represents a particular variable, and each&nbsp;<a title="Row (database)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Row_(database)">row</a>&nbsp;corresponds to a given member of the data set in question. The data set lists values for each of the variables, such as height and weight of an object, for each member of the data set. Each value is known as a datum. The data set may comprise data for one or more members, corresponding to the number of rows.</li>
<li><a title="Data warehouse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_warehouse">Data warehouse</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (DW or DWH), also known as an enterprise data warehouse (EDW), is a system used for&nbsp;<a title="Business reporting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Business_reporting">reporting</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Data analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_analysis">data analysis</a>.&nbsp;DWs are central repositories of integrated data from one or more disparate sources. They store current and historical data in one single place<span style="font-size: xx-small;">.</span></li>
<li><a title="Datalog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Datalog">Datalog</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Declarative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declarative_programming">declarative</a>&nbsp;<a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">logic programming</a>&nbsp;language that syntactically is a subset of&nbsp;<a title="Prolog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prolog">Prolog</a>. It is often used as a&nbsp;<a title="Query language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Query_language">query language</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Deductive database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deductive_database">deductive databases</a>. In recent years, Datalog has found new application in&nbsp;<a title="Data integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_integration">data integration</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information extraction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_extraction">information extraction</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">networking</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Program analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Program_analysis">program analysis</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Security" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Security">security</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Cloud computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_computing">cloud computing</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Decision boundary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_boundary">Decision boundary</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In the case of&nbsp;<a title="Backpropagation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backpropagation">backpropagation</a>&nbsp;based&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Perceptron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perceptron">perceptrons</a>, the type of decision boundary that the network can learn is determined by the number of hidden layers the network has. If it has no hidden layers, then it can only learn linear problems. If it has one hidden layer, then it can learn any&nbsp;<a title="Continuous function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuous_function">continuous function</a>&nbsp;on&nbsp;<a title="Compact space" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compact_space">compact subsets</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Euclidean space" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euclidean_space">R<sup>n</sup></a>&nbsp;as shown by the&nbsp;<a title="Universal approximation theorem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_approximation_theorem">Universal approximation theorem</a>, thus it can have an arbitrary decision boundary.</li>
<li><a title="Decision support system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_support_system">Decision support system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (DSS), is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Information systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_systems">information system</a>&nbsp;that supports business or organizational&nbsp;<a title="Decision-making" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision-making">decision-making</a>&nbsp;activities. DSSs serve the management, operations and planning levels of an organization (usually mid and higher management) and help people make decisions about problems that may be rapidly changing and not easily specified in advance&mdash;i.e. unstructured and semi-structured decision problems. Decision support systems can be either fully computerized or human-powered, or a combination of both.</li>
<li><a title="Decision theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_theory">Decision theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (or the theory of choice) is the study of the reasoning underlying an&nbsp;<a title="Agent (economics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_(economics)">agent's</a>&nbsp;choices.&nbsp;Decision theory can be broken into two branches:&nbsp;<a title="Norm (philosophy)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norm_(philosophy)">normative</a>&nbsp;decision theory, which gives advice on how to make the&nbsp;<a title="Optimal decision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimal_decision">best decisions</a>&nbsp;given a set of uncertain beliefs and a set of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Value (personal and cultural)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(personal_and_cultural)">values</a>, and descriptive decision theory which analyzes how existing, possibly irrational agents actually make decisions.</li>
<li><a title="Decision tree learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_tree_learning">Decision tree learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; uses a&nbsp;<a title="Decision tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_tree">decision tree</a>&nbsp;(as a&nbsp;<a title="Predictive modelling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predictive_modelling">predictive model</a>) to go from observations about an item (represented in the branches) to conclusions about the item's target value (represented in the leaves). It is one of the predictive modeling approaches used in&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data mining</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Declarative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declarative_programming">Declarative programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&mdash;a style of building the structure and elements of computer programs&mdash;that expresses the logic of a&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>&nbsp;without describing its&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">control flow</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Deductive classifier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deductive_classifier">Deductive classifier</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engine</a>. It takes as input a set of declarations in a&nbsp;<a title="Frame language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_language">frame language</a>&nbsp;about a domain such as medical research or molecular biology. For example, the names of&nbsp;<a title="Class hierarchy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_hierarchy">classes, sub-classes</a>, properties, and restrictions on allowable values.</li>
<li><a title="Deep Blue (chess computer)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_Blue_(chess_computer)">Deep Blue</a>&nbsp;&ndash; was a&nbsp;<a title="Computer chess" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_chess">chess-playing computer</a>&nbsp;developed by&nbsp;<a title="IBM" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM">IBM</a>. It is known for being the first computer chess-playing system to win both a chess game and a chess match against a reigning world champion under regular time controls.</li>
<li><a title="Deep learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_learning">Deep learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as deep structured learning or hierarchical learning) is part of a broader family of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;methods based on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Learning representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Learning_representation">learning data representations</a>, as opposed to task-specific algorithms. Learning can be&nbsp;<a title="Supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning">supervised</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Semi-supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-supervised_learning">semi-supervised</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Unsupervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unsupervised_learning">unsupervised</a>.</li>
<li><a title="DeepMind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeepMind">DeepMind</a>&nbsp;&ndash; DeepMind Technologies is a&nbsp;<a title="United Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom">British</a>&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;company founded in September 2010, currently owned by&nbsp;<a title="Alphabet Inc." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphabet_Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a>&nbsp;The company is based in&nbsp;<a title="London" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London">London</a>, with research centres in&nbsp;<a title="Canada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada">Canada</a>,&nbsp;<a title="France" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France">France</a>,&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="United States" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States">United States</a>.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="List of mergers and acquisitions by Google" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Google">Acquired</a>&nbsp;by&nbsp;<a title="Google" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google">Google</a>&nbsp;in 2014, the company has created a&nbsp;<a title="Neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network">neural network</a>&nbsp;that learns how to play&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Video games" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_games">video games</a>&nbsp;in a fashion similar to that of humans,&nbsp;as well as a&nbsp;<a title="Neural Turing machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_Turing_machine">Neural Turing machine</a>,&nbsp;or a neural network that may be able to access an external memory like a conventional&nbsp;<a title="Turing machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_machine">Turing machine</a>, resulting in a computer that mimics the&nbsp;<a title="Short-term memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short-term_memory">short-term memory</a>&nbsp;of the human brain.&nbsp;The company made headlines in 2016 after its&nbsp;<a title="AlphaGo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaGo">AlphaGo</a>&nbsp;program beat a human professional&nbsp;<a title="Go (game)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go_(game)">Go</a>&nbsp;player&nbsp;<a title="Lee Sedol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee_Sedol">Lee Sedol</a>, the world champion, in&nbsp;<a title="AlphaGo versus Lee Sedol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaGo_versus_Lee_Sedol">a five-game match</a>, which was the subject of a documentary film.&nbsp;A more general program,&nbsp;<a title="AlphaZero" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlphaZero">AlphaZero</a>, beat the most powerful programs playing&nbsp;<a title="Go (game)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go_(game)">go</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Chess" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chess">chess</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Shogi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shogi">shogi</a>&nbsp;(Japanese chess) after a few days of play against itself using&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Default logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Default_logic">Default logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Non-monotonic logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-monotonic_logic">non-monotonic logic</a>&nbsp;proposed by&nbsp;<a title="Raymond Reiter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_Reiter">Raymond Reiter</a>&nbsp;to formalize reasoning with default assumptions.</li>
<li><a title="Description logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Description_logic">Description logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Description logics (DL) are a family of formal&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">knowledge representation</a>&nbsp;languages. Many DLs are more expressive than&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Propositional logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_logic">propositional logic</a>&nbsp;but less expressive than&nbsp;<a title="First-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_logic">first-order logic</a>. In contrast to the latter, the core reasoning problems for DLs are (usually)&nbsp;<a title="Decision problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_problem">decidable</a>, and efficient decision procedures have been designed and implemented for these problems. There are general, spatial, temporal, spatiotemporal, and fuzzy descriptions logics, and each description logic features a different balance between DL expressivity and&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge representation and reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation_and_reasoning">reasoning</a>&nbsp;<a title="Complexity class" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complexity_class">complexity</a>&nbsp;by supporting different sets of mathematical constructors.</li>
<li><a title="Developmental robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developmental_robotics">Developmental robotics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (DevRob), sometimes called&nbsp;<a title="Epigenetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epigenetics">epigenetic</a>&nbsp;robotics, is a scientific field which aims at studying the developmental mechanisms, architectures and constraints that allow lifelong and open-ended learning of new skills and new knowledge in embodied&nbsp;<a title="Machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine">machines</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Diagnosis (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diagnosis_(artificial_intelligence)">Diagnosis</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is concerned with the development of algorithms and techniques that are able to determine whether the behaviour of a system is correct. If the system is not functioning correctly, the algorithm should be able to determine, as accurately as possible, which part of the system is failing, and which kind of fault it is facing. The computation is based on&nbsp;<em>observations</em>, which provide information on the current behaviour.</li>
<li><a title="Dialogue system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dialogue_system">Dialogue system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or conversational agent (CA), is a computer system intended to converse with a human with a coherent structure. Dialogue systems have employed text, speech, graphics, haptics, gestures, and other modes for communication on both the input and output channel.</li>
<li><a title="Dimensionality reduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimensionality_reduction">Dimensionality reduction</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or dimension reduction, is the process of reducing the number of random variables under consideration&nbsp;by obtaining a set of principal variables. It can be divided into&nbsp;<a title="Feature selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_selection">feature selection</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Feature extraction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_extraction">feature extraction</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Discrete system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_system">Discrete system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a system with a countable number of states. Discrete systems may be contrasted with continuous systems, which may also be called analog systems. A final discrete system is often modeled with a directed&nbsp;<a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">graph</a>&nbsp;and is analyzed for correctness and complexity according to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computational theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_theory">computational theory</a>. Because discrete systems have a countable number of states, they may be described in precise&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematical models" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_models">mathematical models</a>. A&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Finite state machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finite_state_machine">finite state machine</a>&nbsp;that may be viewed as a discrete system. Because computers are often used to model not only other discrete systems but continuous systems as well, methods have been developed to represent real-world continuous systems as discrete systems. One such method involves sampling a continuous signal at&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Discrete time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_time">discrete time</a>&nbsp;intervals.</li>
<li><a title="Distributed artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_artificial_intelligence">Distributed artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (DAI), also called Decentralized Artificial Intelligence,&nbsp;is a subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;research dedicated to the development of distributed solutions for problems. DAI is closely related to and a predecessor of the field of&nbsp;<a title="Multi-agent system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-agent_system">multi-agent systems</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Dynamic epistemic logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_epistemic_logic">Dynamic epistemic logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (DEL), is a logical framework dealing with knowledge and information change. Typically, DEL focuses on situations involving multiple&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">agents</a>&nbsp;and studies how their knowledge changes when&nbsp;<a title="Event (philosophy)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event_(philosophy)">events</a>&nbsp;occur.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span id="E" class="mw-headline">E</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Eager learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eager_learning">Eager learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a learning method in which the system tries to construct a general, input-independent target function during training of the system, as opposed to&nbsp;<a title="Lazy learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lazy_learning">lazy learning</a>, where generalization beyond the training data is delayed until a query is made to the system.</li>
<li><a title="Ebert test" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebert_test">Ebert test</a>&nbsp;&ndash; gauges whether a computer-based&nbsp;<a title="Speech synthesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_synthesis">synthesized voice</a>&nbsp;can tell a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Humor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humor">joke</a>&nbsp;with sufficient skill to cause people to&nbsp;<a title="Laughter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laughter">laugh</a>.&nbsp;It was proposed by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Film critic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film_critic">film critic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Roger Ebert" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>&nbsp;at the&nbsp;<a title="TED (conference)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)">2011 TED conference</a>&nbsp;as a challenge to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Software developers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_developers">software developers</a>&nbsp;to have a computerized voice master the inflections, delivery, timing, and intonations of a speaking human.&nbsp;The test is similar to the&nbsp;<a title="Turing test" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test">Turing test</a>&nbsp;proposed by&nbsp;<a title="Alan Turing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Turing">Alan Turing</a>&nbsp;in 1950 as a way to gauge a computer's ability to exhibit intelligent behavior by generating performance indistinguishable from a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human being" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_being">human being</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Echo state network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Echo_state_network">Echo state network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The echo state network (ESN),&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network">recurrent neural network</a>&nbsp;with a sparsely connected hidden layer (with typically 1% connectivity). The connectivity and weights of hidden&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neuron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neuron">neurons</a>&nbsp;are fixed and randomly assigned. The weights of output neurons can be learned so that the network can (re)produce specific temporal patterns. The main interest of this network is that although its behaviour is non-linear, the only weights that are modified during training are for the synapses that connect the hidden neurons to output neurons. Thus, the error function is quadratic with respect to the parameter vector and can be differentiated easily to a linear system.</li>
<li><a title="Embodied agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embodied_agent">Embodied agent</a>&nbsp;&ndash; also sometimes referred to as an interface agent,&nbsp;is an&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agent</a>&nbsp;that interacts with the environment through a physical body within that environment. Agents that are represented graphically with a body, for example a human or a cartoon animal, are also called embodied agents, although they have only virtual, not physical, embodiment.</li>
<li><a title="Embodied cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embodied_cognitive_science">Embodied cognitive science</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an interdisciplinary field of research, the aim of which is to explain the mechanisms underlying intelligent behavior. It comprises three main methodologies: 1) the modeling of psychological and biological systems in a holistic manner that considers the mind and body as a single entity, 2) the formation of a common set of general principles of intelligent behavior, and 3) the experimental use of robotic agents in controlled environments.</li>
<li><a title="Error-driven learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Error-driven_learning">Error-driven learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a sub-area of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;concerned with how an&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">agent</a>&nbsp;ought to take actions in an&nbsp;<a title="Environment (systems)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(systems)">environment</a>&nbsp;so as to minimize some error feedback. It is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Ensemble averaging (machine learning)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ensemble_averaging_(machine_learning)">Ensemble averaging</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, particularly in the creation of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_networks">artificial neural networks</a>, ensemble averaging is the process of creating multiple models and combining them to produce a desired output, as opposed to creating just one model.</li>
<li><a title="Ethics of artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics_of_artificial_intelligence">Ethics of artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the part of the&nbsp;<a title="Ethics of technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics_of_technology">ethics of technology</a>&nbsp;specific to artificial intelligence.</li>
<li><a title="Evolutionary algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_algorithm">Evolutionary algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (EA), is a&nbsp;<a title="Subset" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subset">subset</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation">evolutionary computation</a>,&nbsp;a generic population-based&nbsp;<a title="Metaheuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaheuristic">metaheuristic</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Optimization (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_(mathematics)">optimization</a>&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>. An EA uses mechanisms inspired by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_evolution">biological evolution</a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reproduction">reproduction</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Mutation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation">mutation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Genetic recombination" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_recombination">recombination</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Natural selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_selection">selection</a>.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Candidate solution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Candidate_solution">Candidate solutions</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Optimization problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_problem">optimization problem</a>&nbsp;play the role of individuals in a population, and the&nbsp;<a title="Fitness function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitness_function">fitness function</a>&nbsp;determines the quality of the solutions.&nbsp;<a title="Evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolution">Evolution</a>&nbsp;of the population then takes place after the repeated application of the above operators.</li>
<li><a title="Evolutionary computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation">Evolutionary computation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a family of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Global optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_optimization">global optimization</a>&nbsp;inspired by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_evolution">biological evolution</a>, and the subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Soft computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soft_computing">soft computing</a>&nbsp;studying these algorithms. In technical terms, they are a family of population-based&nbsp;<a title="Trial and error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trial_and_error">trial and error</a>&nbsp;problem solvers with a&nbsp;<a title="Metaheuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaheuristic">metaheuristic</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_optimization">stochastic optimization</a>&nbsp;character.</li>
<li><a title="Evolving classification function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolving_classification_function">Evolving classification function</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (ECF), evolving classifier functions or evolving&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Classifier (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classifier_(mathematics)">classifiers</a>&nbsp;are used for classifying and clustering in the field of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, typically employed for&nbsp;<a title="Data stream mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_stream_mining">data stream mining</a>&nbsp;tasks in dynamic and changing environments.</li>
<li><a title="Existential risk from artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existential_risk_from_artificial_general_intelligence">Existential risk</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the hypothesis that substantial progress in&nbsp;<a title="Artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence">artificial general intelligence</a>&nbsp;(AGI) could someday result in&nbsp;<a title="Human extinction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_extinction">human extinction</a>&nbsp;or some other unrecoverable&nbsp;<a title="Global catastrophic risk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_catastrophic_risk">global catastrophe</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Expert system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_system">Expert system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a computer system that emulates the decision-making ability of a human expert.&nbsp;Expert systems are designed to solve complex problems by&nbsp;<a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">reasoning</a>&nbsp;through bodies of knowledge, represented mainly as&nbsp;<a title="Rule-based system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule-based_system">if&ndash;then rules</a>&nbsp;rather than through conventional&nbsp;<a title="Procedural programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedural_programming">procedural code</a>.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span id="F" class="mw-headline">F</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Fast-and-frugal trees" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast-and-frugal_trees">Fast-and-frugal trees</a>&nbsp;&ndash; a type of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Classification tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classification_tree">classification tree</a>. Fast-and-frugal trees can be used as decision-making tools which operate as lexicographic classifiers, and, if required, associate an action (decision) to each class or category.</li>
<li><a title="Feature extraction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_extraction">Feature extraction</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pattern recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_recognition">pattern recognition</a>&nbsp;and in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Image processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_processing">image processing</a>, feature extraction starts from an initial set of measured data and builds derived values (<a title="Feature (machine learning)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_(machine_learning)">features</a>) intended to be informative and non-redundant, facilitating the subsequent learning and generalization steps, and in some cases leading to better human interpretations.</li>
<li><a title="Feature learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_learning">Feature learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, feature learning or representation learning&nbsp;is a set of techniques that allows a system to automatically discover the representations needed for feature detection or classification from raw data. This replaces manual&nbsp;<a title="Feature engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_engineering">feature engineering</a>&nbsp;and allows a machine to both learn the features and use them to perform a specific task.</li>
<li><a title="Feature selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_selection">Feature selection</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>, feature selection, also known as variable selection, attribute selection or variable subset selection, is the process of selecting a subset of relevant&nbsp;<a title="Feature (machine learning)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_(machine_learning)">features</a>&nbsp;(variables, predictors) for use in model construction.</li>
<li><a title="Federated learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federated_learning">Federated learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; a type of machine learning that allows for training on multiple devices with decentralized data, thus helping preserve the privacy of individual users and their data.</li>
<li><a title="First-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_logic">First-order logic</a>&nbsp;(also known as first-order predicate calculus and predicate logic) &ndash; a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Formal system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_system">formal systems</a>&nbsp;used in&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Philosophy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">philosophy</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>. First-order logic uses&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Quantification (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantification_(logic)">quantified variables</a>&nbsp;over non-logical objects and allows the use of sentences that contain variables, so that rather than propositions such as&nbsp;<em>Socrates is a man</em>&nbsp;one can have expressions in the form "there exists X such that X is&nbsp;<a title="Socrates" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socrates">Socrates</a>&nbsp;and X is a man" and&nbsp;<em>there exists</em>&nbsp;is a quantifier while&nbsp;<em>X</em>&nbsp;is a variable.&nbsp;This distinguishes it from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Propositional logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_logic">propositional logic</a>, which does not use quantifiers or relations.</li>
<li><a title="Fluent (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fluent_(artificial_intelligence)">Fluent</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;a condition that can change over time. In&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logical</a>&nbsp;approaches to reasoning about actions, fluents can be represented in&nbsp;<a title="First-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_logic">first-order logic</a>&nbsp;by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Predicate (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predicate_(logic)">predicates</a>&nbsp;having an argument that depends on time.</li>
<li><a title="Formal language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_language">Formal language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; a set of&nbsp;<a title="String (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/String_(computer_science)">words</a>&nbsp;whose&nbsp;<a title="Symbol (formal)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbol_(formal)">letters</a>&nbsp;are taken from an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Alphabet (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphabet_(computer_science)">alphabet</a>&nbsp;and are&nbsp;<a title="Well-formedness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Well-formedness">well-formed</a>&nbsp;according to a specific set of rules.</li>
<li><a title="Forward chaining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forward_chaining">Forward chaining</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (or forward reasoning) is one of the two main methods of reasoning when using an&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engine</a>&nbsp;and can be described&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Logically" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logically">logically</a>&nbsp;as repeated application of&nbsp;<em><a title="Modus ponens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modus_ponens">modus ponens</a></em>. Forward chaining is a popular implementation strategy for&nbsp;<a title="Expert system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_system">expert systems</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Business rules engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Business_rules_engine">business</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Production system (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Production_system_(computer_science)">production rule systems</a>. The opposite of forward chaining is&nbsp;<a title="Backward chaining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backward_chaining">backward chaining</a>. Forward chaining starts with the available&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>&nbsp;and uses inference rules to extract more data (from an end user, for example) until a&nbsp;<a title="Goal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal">goal</a>&nbsp;is reached. An&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engine</a>&nbsp;using forward chaining searches the inference rules until it finds one where the&nbsp;<a title="Antecedent (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antecedent_(logic)">antecedent</a>&nbsp;(If clause) is known to be true. When such a rule is found, the engine can conclude, or infer, the&nbsp;<a title="Consequent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consequent">consequent</a>&nbsp;(Then clause), resulting in the addition of new&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>&nbsp;to its data.</li>
<li><a title="Frame (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_(artificial_intelligence)">Frame</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;an artificial intelligence&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;used to divide&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge">knowledge</a>&nbsp;into substructures by representing "<a title="Stereotype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stereotype">stereotyped</a>&nbsp;situations." Frames are the primary data structure used in artificial intelligence&nbsp;<a title="Frame language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_language">frame language</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Frame language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_language">Frame language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; a technology used for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">knowledge representation</a>&nbsp;in artificial intelligence. Frames are stored as&nbsp;<a title="Ontology (information science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_(information_science)">ontologies</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">sets</a>&nbsp;and subsets of the&nbsp;<a title="Frame (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_(artificial_intelligence)">frame concepts</a>. They are similar to class hierarchies in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Object-oriented languages" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_languages">object-oriented languages</a>&nbsp;although their fundamental design goals are different. Frames are focused on explicit and intuitive representation of knowledge whereas objects focus on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Encapsulation (object-oriented programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encapsulation_(object-oriented_programming)">encapsulation</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Information hiding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_hiding">information hiding</a>. Frames originated in AI research and objects primarily in&nbsp;<a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">software engineering</a>. However, in practice the techniques and capabilities of frame and object-oriented languages overlap significantly.</li>
<li><a title="Frame problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_problem">Frame problem</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the problem of finding adequate collections of axioms for a viable description of a robot environment.</li>
<li><a title="Friendly artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friendly_artificial_intelligence">Friendly artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;(also friendly AI or FAI) &ndash; a hypothetical&nbsp;<a title="Artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence">artificial general intelligence</a>&nbsp;(AGI) that would have a positive effect on humanity. It is a part of the&nbsp;<a title="Ethics of artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics_of_artificial_intelligence">ethics of artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and is closely related to&nbsp;<a title="Machine ethics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_ethics">machine ethics</a>. While machine ethics is concerned with how an artificially intelligent agent should behave, friendly artificial intelligence research is focused on how to practically bring about this behaviour and ensuring it is adequately constrained.</li>
<li><a title="Futures studies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futures_studies">Futures studies</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of postulating possible, probable, and preferable&nbsp;<a title="Future" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Future">futures</a>&nbsp;and the worldviews and myths that underlie them.</li>
<li><a title="Fuzzy control system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_control_system">Fuzzy control system</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;a&nbsp;<a title="Control system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_system">control system</a>&nbsp;based on&nbsp;<a title="Fuzzy logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_logic">fuzzy logic</a>&mdash;a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematical</a>&nbsp;system that analyzes&nbsp;<a title="Analog signal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analog_signal">analog</a>&nbsp;input values in terms of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">logical</a>&nbsp;variables that take on continuous values between 0 and 1, in contrast to classical or&nbsp;<a title="Digital data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_data">digital</a>&nbsp;logic, which operates on discrete values of either 1 or 0 (true or false, respectively).</li>
<li><a title="Fuzzy logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_logic">Fuzzy logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;a simple form for the&nbsp;<a title="Many-valued logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Many-valued_logic">many-valued logic</a>, in which the&nbsp;<a title="Truth value" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truth_value">truth values</a>&nbsp;of variables may have any degree of "<em>Truthfulness</em>" that can be represented by any real number in the range between 0 (as in Completely False) and 1 (as in Completely True) inclusive. Consequently, It is employed to handle the concept of partial truth, where the truth value may range between completely true and completely false. In contrast to&nbsp;<a title="Boolean algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_algebra">Boolean logic</a>, where the truth values of variables may have the integer values 0 or 1 only.</li>
<li><a title="Fuzzy rule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_rule">Fuzzy rule</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Fuzzy rules are used within&nbsp;<a title="Fuzzy logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_logic">fuzzy logic systems</a>&nbsp;to infer an output based on input variables.</li>
<li><a title="Fuzzy set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_set">Fuzzy set</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In classical&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">set theory</a>, the membership of elements in a set is assessed in binary terms according to a&nbsp;<a title="Principle of bivalence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principle_of_bivalence">bivalent condition</a>&nbsp;&mdash; an element either belongs or does not belong to the set. By contrast, fuzzy set theory permits the gradual assessment of the membership of elements in a set; this is described with the aid of a&nbsp;<a title="Membership function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Membership_function_(mathematics)">membership function</a>&nbsp;valued in the real unit interval [0,&nbsp;1]. Fuzzy sets generalize classical sets, since the&nbsp;<a title="Indicator function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indicator_function">indicator functions</a>&nbsp;(aka characteristic functions) of classical sets are special cases of the membership functions of fuzzy sets, if the latter only take values 0 or 1.&nbsp;In fuzzy set theory, classical bivalent sets are usually called&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Crisp set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crisp_set"><em>crisp</em>&nbsp;sets</a>. The fuzzy set theory can be used in a wide range of domains in which information is incomplete or imprecise, such as&nbsp;<a title="Bioinformatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioinformatics">bioinformatics</a>.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span id="G" class="mw-headline">G</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Game theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory">Game theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical models</a>&nbsp;of strategic interaction between rational decision-makers.</li>
<li><a title="Generative adversarial network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_adversarial_network">Generative adversarial network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (GAN), is a class of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;systems. Two&nbsp;<a title="Neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network">neural networks</a>&nbsp;contest with each other in a&nbsp;<a title="Zero-sum game" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero-sum_game">zero-sum game</a>&nbsp;framework.</li>
<li><a title="Genetic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithm">Genetic algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (GA), is a&nbsp;<a title="Metaheuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaheuristic">metaheuristic</a>&nbsp;inspired by the process of&nbsp;<a title="Natural selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_selection">natural selection</a>&nbsp;that belongs to the larger class of&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_algorithm">evolutionary algorithms</a>&nbsp;(EA). Genetic algorithms are commonly used to generate high-quality solutions to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Optimization (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_(mathematics)">optimization</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search problems</a>&nbsp;by relying on bio-inspired operators such as&nbsp;<a title="Mutation (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation_(genetic_algorithm)">mutation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Crossover (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossover_(genetic_algorithm)">crossover</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Selection (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selection_(genetic_algorithm)">selection</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Genetic operator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_operator">Genetic operator</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Operator (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operator_(programming)">operator</a>&nbsp;used in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithms">genetic algorithms</a>&nbsp;to guide the algorithm towards a solution to a given problem. There are three main types of operators (<a title="Mutation (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation_(genetic_algorithm)">mutation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Crossover (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossover_(genetic_algorithm)">crossover</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Selection (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selection_(genetic_algorithm)">selection</a>), which must work in conjunction with one another in order for the algorithm to be successful.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Glowworm swarm optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glowworm_swarm_optimization">Glowworm swarm optimization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Swarm intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swarm_intelligence">swarm intelligence</a>&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization">optimization</a>&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;developed based on the behaviour of&nbsp;<a title="Glowworm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glowworm">glowworms</a>&nbsp;(also known as fireflies or lightning bugs).</li>
<li><a title="Graph (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(abstract_data_type)">Graph (abstract data type)</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, a graph is an&nbsp;<a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">abstract data type</a>&nbsp;that is meant to implement the&nbsp;<a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">undirected graph</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Directed graph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directed_graph">directed graph</a>&nbsp;concepts from&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>; specifically, the field of&nbsp;<a title="Graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory">graph theory</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">Graph (discrete mathematics)</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>, and more specifically in&nbsp;<a title="Graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory">graph theory</a>, a graph is a structure amounting to a set of objects in which some pairs of the objects are in some sense "related". The objects correspond to mathematical abstractions called&nbsp;<em><a title="Vertex (graph theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertex_(graph_theory)">vertices</a></em>&nbsp;(also called&nbsp;<em>nodes</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>points</em>) and each of the related pairs of vertices is called an&nbsp;<em>edge</em>&nbsp;(also called an&nbsp;<em>arc</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>line</em>).</li>
<li><a title="Graph database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_database">Graph database</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (GDB), is a&nbsp;<a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database">database</a>&nbsp;that uses&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Graph (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(data_structure)">graph structures</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Semantic query" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_query">semantic queries</a>&nbsp;with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Node (graph theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(graph_theory)">nodes</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Edge (graph theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edge_(graph_theory)">edges</a>&nbsp;and properties to represent and store data. A key concept of the system is the&nbsp;<em>graph</em>&nbsp;(or&nbsp;<em>edge</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>relationship</em>), which directly relates data items in the store a collection of nodes of data and edges representing the relationships between the nodes. The relationships allow data in the store to be linked together directly, and in many cases retrieved with one operation. Graph databases hold the relationships between data as a priority. Querying relationships within a graph database is fast because they are perpetually stored within the database itself. Relationships can be intuitively visualized using graph databases, making it useful for heavily inter-connected data.</li>
<li><a title="Graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory">Graph theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of&nbsp;<em><a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">graphs</a></em>, which are mathematical structures used to model pairwise relations between objects.</li>
<li><a title="Graph traversal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_traversal">Graph traversal</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as graph search) refers to the process of visiting (checking and/or updating) each vertex in a&nbsp;<a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">graph</a>. Such traversals are classified by the order in which the vertices are visited.&nbsp;<a title="Tree traversal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_traversal">Tree traversal</a>&nbsp;is a special case of graph traversal.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="H" class="mw-headline">H</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Heuristic (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heuristic_(computer_science)">Heuristic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a technique designed for&nbsp;<a title="Problem solving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problem_solving">solving a problem</a>&nbsp;more quickly when classic methods are too slow, or for finding an approximate solution when classic methods fail to find any exact solution. This is achieved by trading optimality, completeness,&nbsp;<a title="Accuracy and precision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accuracy_and_precision">accuracy</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Accuracy and precision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accuracy_and_precision">precision</a>&nbsp;for speed. In a way, it can be considered a shortcut. A heuristic function, also called simply a heuristic, is a&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>&nbsp;that ranks alternatives in&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search algorithms</a>&nbsp;at each branching step based on available information to decide which branch to follow. For example, it may approximate the exact solution.</li>
<li><span id="hidden_layer"></span>Hidden layer &ndash; an internal layer of neurons in an&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>, not dedicated to input or output</li>
<li><span id="hidden_unit"></span>Hidden unit &ndash; an neuron in a hidden layer in an&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a></li>
<li><a title="Hyper-heuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyper-heuristic">Hyper-heuristic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Heuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heuristic">heuristic</a>&nbsp;search method that seeks to automate, often by the incorporation of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;techniques, the process of selecting, combining, generating or adapting several simpler heuristics (or components of such heuristics) to efficiently solve computational search problems. One of the motivations for studying hyper-heuristics is to build systems which can handle classes of problems rather than solving just one problem.</li>
</ul>


<h2><span id="I" class="mw-headline">I</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="IEEE Computational Intelligence Society" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IEEE_Computational_Intelligence_Society">IEEE Computational Intelligence Society</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Professional society" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_society">professional society</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers">Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers</a>&nbsp;(IEEE) focussing on "the theory, design, application, and development of biologically and linguistically motivated computational paradigms emphasizing&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_networks">neural networks</a>, connectionist systems,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithms">genetic algorithms</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_programming">evolutionary programming</a>, fuzzy systems, and hybrid intelligent systems in which these paradigms are contained".</li>
<li><a title="Incremental learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incremental_learning">Incremental learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a method of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, in which input data is continuously used to extend the existing model's knowledge i.e. to further train the model. It represents a dynamic technique of&nbsp;<a title="Supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning">supervised learning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Unsupervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unsupervised_learning">unsupervised learning</a>&nbsp;that can be applied when training data becomes available gradually over time or its size is out of system memory limits. Algorithms that can facilitate incremental learning are known as incremental machine learning algorithms.</li>
<li><a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">Inference engine</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a component of the system that applies logical rules to the knowledge base to deduce new information.</li>
<li><a title="Information integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_integration">Information integration</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (II), is the merging of information from heterogeneous sources with differing conceptual, contextual and typographical representations. It is used in&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data mining</a>&nbsp;and consolidation of data from unstructured or semi-structured resources. Typically,&nbsp;<em>information integration</em>&nbsp;refers to textual representations of knowledge but is sometimes applied to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Rich-media" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rich-media">rich-media</a>&nbsp;content. Information fusion, which is a related term, involves the combination of information into a new set of information towards reducing redundancy and uncertainty.</li>
<li><a title="Information Processing Language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Processing_Language">Information Processing Language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (IPL), is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;that includes features intended to help with programs that perform simple problem solving actions such as lists,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Dynamic memory allocation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_memory_allocation">dynamic memory allocation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">data types</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Recursion (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recursion_(computer_science)">recursion</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">functions</a>&nbsp;as arguments, generators, and&nbsp;<a title="Cooperative multitasking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooperative_multitasking">cooperative multitasking</a>. IPL invented the concept of list processing, albeit in an&nbsp;<a title="Assembly language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_language">assembly-language</a>&nbsp;style.</li>
<li><a title="Intelligence amplification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence_amplification">Intelligence amplification</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (IA), (also referred to as cognitive augmentation, machine augmented intelligence and enhanced intelligence), refers to the effective use of&nbsp;<a title="Information technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_technology">information technology</a>&nbsp;in augmenting&nbsp;<a title="Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence#Human_intelligence">human intelligence</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Intelligence explosion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence_explosion">Intelligence explosion</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a possible outcome of humanity building&nbsp;<a title="Artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence">artificial general intelligence</a>&nbsp;(AGI). AGI would be capable of recursive self-improvement leading to rapid emergence of ASI (<a title="Superintelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superintelligence">artificial superintelligence</a>), the limits of which are unknown, at the time of the technological singularity.</li>
<li><a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">Intelligent agent</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (IA), is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous">autonomous</a>&nbsp;entity which acts, directing its activity towards achieving goals (i.e. it is an&nbsp;<a title="Software agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_agent">agent</a>), upon an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Environment (biophysical)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)">environment</a>&nbsp;using observation through sensors and consequent actuators (i.e. it is intelligent). Intelligent agents may also&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">learn</a>&nbsp;or use&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">knowledge</a>&nbsp;to achieve their goals. They may be very simple or&nbsp;<a title="Complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complexity">very complex</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Intelligent control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_control">Intelligent control</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a class of&nbsp;<a title="Control theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_theory">control</a>&nbsp;techniques that use various&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;computing approaches like&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_networks">neural networks</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Bayesian probability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayesian_probability">Bayesian probability</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Fuzzy logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_logic">fuzzy logic</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation">evolutionary computation</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Genetic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithm">genetic algorithms</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Intelligent personal assistant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_personal_assistant">Intelligent personal assistant</a>&nbsp;&ndash; A virtual assistant or intelligent personal assistant is a&nbsp;<a title="Software agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_agent">software agent</a>&nbsp;that can perform tasks or services for an individual based on verbal commands. Sometimes the term "<a title="Chatbot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chatbot">chatbot</a>" is used to refer to virtual assistants generally or specifically accessed by&nbsp;<a title="Online chat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Online_chat">online chat</a>&nbsp;(or in some cases online chat programs that are exclusively for entertainment purposes). Some virtual assistants are able to interpret human speech and respond via synthesized voices. Users can ask their assistants questions, control home automation devices and media playback via voice, and manage other basic tasks such as email, to-do lists, and calendars with verbal commands.</li>
<li><a title="Interpretation (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpretation_(logic)">Interpretation (logic)</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an assignment of meaning to the&nbsp;<a title="Symbol (formal)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbol_(formal)">symbols</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Formal language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_language">formal language</a>. Many formal languages used in&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>&nbsp;are defined in solely&nbsp;<a title="Syntax" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syntax">syntactic</a>&nbsp;terms, and as such do not have any meaning until they are given some interpretation. The general study of interpretations of formal languages is called&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal semantics (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_semantics_(logic)">formal semantics</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Issue tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Issue_tree">Issue tree</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Also called logic tree, is a graphical breakdown of a question that dissects it into its different components vertically and that progresses into details as it reads to the right.&nbsp;Issue trees are useful in&nbsp;<a title="Problem solving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problem_solving">problem solving</a>&nbsp;to identify the root causes of a problem as well as to identify its potential solutions. They also provide a reference point to see how each piece fits into the whole picture of a problem.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span id="J" class="mw-headline">J</span></h2>
<ul>
