<li><a title="Junction tree algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Junction_tree_algorithm">Junction tree algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as 'Clique Tree') is a method used in&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;to extract&nbsp;<a title="Marginal distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marginal_distribution">marginalization</a>&nbsp;in general&nbsp;<a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">graphs</a>. In essence, it entails performing&nbsp;<a title="Belief propagation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belief_propagation">belief propagation</a>&nbsp;on a modified graph called a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Junction tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Junction_tree">junction tree</a>. The graph is called a tree because it branches into different sections of data;&nbsp;<a title="Vertex (graph theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertex_(graph_theory)">nodes</a>&nbsp;of variables are the branches.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="K" class="mw-headline">K</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Kernel method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kernel_method">Kernel method</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, kernel methods are a class of algorithms for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Pattern analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_analysis">pattern analysis</a>, whose best known member is the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Support vector machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Support_vector_machine">support vector machine</a>&nbsp;(SVM). The general task of pattern analysis is to find and study general types of relations (for example&nbsp;<a title="Cluster analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cluster_analysis">clusters</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Ranking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranking">rankings</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Principal components" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principal_components">principal components</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Correlation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Correlation">correlations</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">classifications</a>) in datasets.</li>
<li><a title="KL-ONE" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KL-ONE">KL-ONE</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a well known&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">knowledge representation</a>&nbsp;system in the tradition of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Semantic networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_networks">semantic networks</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Frame (Artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_(Artificial_intelligence)">frames</a>; that is, it is a&nbsp;<a title="Frame language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_language">frame language</a>. The system is an attempt to overcome semantic indistinctness in semantic network representations and to explicitly represent conceptual information as a structured inheritance network.</li>
<li><a title="Knowledge acquisition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_acquisition">Knowledge acquisition</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process used to define the rules and ontologies required for a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge-based system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge-based_system">knowledge-based system</a>. The phrase was first used in conjunction with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Expert systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_systems">expert systems</a>&nbsp;to describe the initial tasks associated with developing an expert system, namely finding and interviewing&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge domain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_domain">domain</a>&nbsp;experts and capturing their knowledge via&nbsp;<a title="Rule-based system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule-based_system">rules</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">objects</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Frame language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_language">frame-based</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ontologies (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontologies_(computer_science)">ontologies</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Knowledge-based systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge-based_systems">Knowledge-based systems</a>&nbsp;&ndash; A knowledge-based system (KBS) is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;that&nbsp;<a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">reasons</a>&nbsp;and uses a&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_base">knowledge base</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a title="Problem solving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problem_solving">solve</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Complex systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_systems">complex problems</a>. The term is broad and refers to many different kinds of systems. The one common theme that unites all knowledge based systems is an attempt to represent knowledge explicitly and a&nbsp;<a title="Reasoning system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning_system">reasoning system</a>&nbsp;that allows it to derive new knowledge. Thus, a knowledge-based system has two distinguishing features: a&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_base">knowledge base</a>&nbsp;and an&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engine</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Knowledge engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_engineering">Knowledge engineering</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (KE) refers to all technical, scientific and social aspects involved in building, maintaining and using&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge-based systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge-based_systems">knowledge-based systems</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Knowledge extraction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_extraction">Knowledge extraction</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the creation of&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge representation and reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation_and_reasoning">knowledge</a>&nbsp;from structured (<a class="mw-redirect" title="Relational databases" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relational_databases">relational databases</a>,&nbsp;<a title="XML" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XML">XML</a>) and unstructured (<a title="Text (literary theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Text_(literary_theory)">text</a>, documents,&nbsp;<a title="Image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image">images</a>) sources. The resulting knowledge needs to be in a machine-readable and machine-interpretable format and must&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge representation and reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation_and_reasoning">represent knowledge</a>&nbsp;in a manner that facilitates inferencing. Although it is methodically similar to&nbsp;<a title="Information extraction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_extraction">information extraction</a>&nbsp;(<a title="Natural language processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing">NLP</a>) and&nbsp;<a title="Extract, transform, load" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extract,_transform,_load">ETL</a>&nbsp;(data warehouse), the main criteria is that the extraction result goes beyond the creation of structured information or the transformation into a&nbsp;<a title="Database schema" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_schema">relational schema</a>. It requires either the reuse of existing&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge representation and reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation_and_reasoning">formal knowledge</a>&nbsp;(reusing identifiers or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ontologies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontologies">ontologies</a>) or the generation of a schema based on the source data.</li>
<li><a title="Knowledge Interchange Format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_Interchange_Format">Knowledge Interchange Format</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (KIF) is a computer language designed to enable systems to share and re-use information from&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge-based systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge-based_systems">knowledge-based systems</a>. KIF is similar to&nbsp;<a title="Frame language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_language">frame languages</a>&nbsp;such as&nbsp;<a title="KL-ONE" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KL-ONE">KL-ONE</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="LOOM (ontology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LOOM_(ontology)">LOOM</a>&nbsp;but unlike such language its primary role is not intended as a framework for the expression or use of knowledge but rather for the interchange of knowledge between systems. The designers of KIF likened it to&nbsp;<a title="PostScript" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PostScript">PostScript</a>. PostScript was not designed primarily as a language to store and manipulate documents but rather as an interchange format for systems and devices to share documents. In the same way KIF is meant to facilitate sharing of knowledge across different systems that use different languages, formalisms, platforms, etc.</li>
<li><a title="Knowledge representation and reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation_and_reasoning">Knowledge representation and reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (KR&sup2;, KR&amp;R) is the field of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;(AI) dedicated to representing information about the world in a form that a computer system can utilize to solve complex tasks such as&nbsp;<a title="Computer-aided diagnosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer-aided_diagnosis">diagnosing a medical condition</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language user interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_user_interface">having a dialog in a natural language</a>. Knowledge representation incorporates findings from psychology about how humans solve problems and represent knowledge in order to design&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formalism (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formalism_(mathematics)">formalisms</a>&nbsp;that will make complex systems easier to design and build. Knowledge representation and reasoning also incorporates findings from&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>&nbsp;to automate various kinds of&nbsp;<em>reasoning</em>, such as the application of rules or the relations of&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">sets</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Subset" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subset">subsets</a>.&nbsp;Examples of knowledge representation formalisms include&nbsp;<a title="Semantic network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_network">semantic nets</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Systems architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_architecture">systems architecture</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Frame (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_(artificial_intelligence)">frames</a>, rules, and&nbsp;<a title="Ontology (information science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_(information_science)">ontologies</a>. Examples of&nbsp;<a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">automated reasoning</a>&nbsp;engines include&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engines</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Automated theorem proving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_theorem_proving">theorem provers</a>, and classifiers.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="L" class="mw-headline">L</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Lazy learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lazy_learning">Lazy learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, lazy learning is a learning method in which generalization of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Training data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Training_data">training data</a>&nbsp;is, in theory, delayed until a query is made to the system, as opposed to in&nbsp;<a title="Eager learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eager_learning">eager learning</a>, where the system tries to generalize the training data before receiving queries.</li>
<li><a title="Lisp (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lisp_(programming_language)">Lisp (programming language)</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (historically LISP), is a family of&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming languages</a>&nbsp;with a long history and a distinctive, fully&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Parenthesized" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parenthesized">parenthesized</a>&nbsp;<a title="Polish notation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_notation#Computer_programming">prefix notation</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">Logic programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;which is largely based on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_logic">formal logic</a>. Any program written in a logic&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;is a set of sentences in logical form, expressing facts and rules about some problem domain. Major logic programming language families include&nbsp;<a title="Prolog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prolog">Prolog</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Answer set programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Answer_set_programming">Answer set programming</a>&nbsp;(ASP) and&nbsp;<a title="Datalog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Datalog">Datalog</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Long short-term memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_short-term_memory">Long short-term memory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (LSTM), is an artificial&nbsp;<a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network">recurrent neural network</a>, (RNN) architecture&nbsp;used in the field of&nbsp;<a title="Deep learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_learning">deep learning</a>. Unlike standard&nbsp;<a title="Feedforward neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feedforward_neural_network">feedforward neural networks</a>, LSTM has feedback connections that make it a "general purpose computer" (that is, it can compute anything that a&nbsp;<a title="Turing machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_machine">Turing machine</a>&nbsp;can).&nbsp;It can not only process single data points (such as images), but also entire sequences of data (such as speech or video).</li>
</ul>

<h2><span id="M" class="mw-headline">M</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Machine vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_vision">Machine vision</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (MV) is the technology and methods used to provide imaging-based automatic inspection and analysis for such applications as automatic inspection,&nbsp;<a title="Process control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Process_control">process control</a>, and robot guidance, usually in industry. Machine vision is a term encompassing a large number of technologies, software and hardware products, integrated systems, actions, methods and expertise. Machine vision as a&nbsp;<a title="Systems engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_engineering">systems engineering</a>&nbsp;discipline can be considered distinct from&nbsp;<a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">computer vision</a>, a form of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>. It attempts to integrate existing technologies in new ways and apply them to solve real world problems. The term is the prevalent one for these functions in industrial automation environments but is also used for these functions in other environments such as security and vehicle guidance.</li>
<li><a title="Markov chain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_chain">Markov chain</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Stochastic model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_model">stochastic model</a>&nbsp;describing a&nbsp;<a title="Sequence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sequence">sequence</a>&nbsp;of possible events in which the probability of each event depends only on the state attained in the previous event.</li>
<li><a title="Markov decision process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_decision_process">Markov decision process</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (MDP) is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Discrete time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_time">discrete time</a>&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic">stochastic</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Optimal control theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimal_control_theory">control</a>&nbsp;process. It provides a mathematical framework for modeling&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Decision making" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_making">decision making</a>&nbsp;in situations where outcomes are partly&nbsp;<a title="Randomness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Randomness#In_mathematics">random</a>&nbsp;and partly under the control of a decision maker. MDPs are useful for studying&nbsp;<a title="Optimization problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_problem">optimization problems</a>&nbsp;solved via&nbsp;<a title="Dynamic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_programming">dynamic programming</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Mathematical optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization">Mathematical optimization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Operations research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operations_research">operations research</a>, mathematical optimization (alternatively spelled&nbsp;<em>optimisation</em>) or mathematical programming is the selection of a best element (with regard to some criterion) from some set of available alternatives.</li>
<li><a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">Machine learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (ML) is the&nbsp;<a title="Branches of science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branches_of_science">scientific study</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Statistical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_model">statistical models</a>&nbsp;that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_systems">computer systems</a>&nbsp;use in order to perform a specific task effectively without using explicit instructions, relying on patterns and inference instead.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Machine listening" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_listening">Machine listening</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Computer audition (CA) or machine listening is general field of study of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;and systems for audio understanding by machine.</li>
<li><a title="Machine perception" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_perception">Machine perception</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the capability of a computer system to interpret data in a manner that is similar to the way humans use their senses to relate to the world around them.</li>
<li><a title="Mechanism design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanism_design">Mechanism design</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a field in&nbsp;<a title="Economics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economics">economics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Game theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory">game theory</a>&nbsp;that takes an&nbsp;<a title="Engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering">engineering</a>&nbsp;approach to designing economic mechanisms or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Economic incentive" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_incentive">incentives</a>, toward desired objectives, in&nbsp;<a title="Strategy (game theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategy_(game_theory)">strategic settings</a>, where players act&nbsp;<a title="Rational choice theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rational_choice_theory">rationally</a>. Because it starts at the end of the game, then goes backwards, it is also called reverse game theory. It has broad applications, from economics and politics (markets, auctions, voting procedures) to networked-systems (internet interdomain routing, sponsored search auctions).</li>
<li><a title="Mechatronics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechatronics">Mechatronics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; which is also called mechatronic engineering, is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Multidisciplinary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multidisciplinary">multidisciplinary</a>&nbsp;branch of engineering that focuses on the engineering of both&nbsp;<a title="Electrical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_engineering">electrical</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mechanical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanical_engineering">mechanical systems</a>, and also includes a combination of&nbsp;<a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">robotics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Electronics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronics">electronics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_engineering">computer</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Systems engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_engineering">systems</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Control engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_engineering">control</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Product engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_engineering">product</a>&nbsp;engineering.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Metabolic network reconstruction and simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metabolic_network_reconstruction_and_simulation">Metabolic network reconstruction and simulation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; allows for an in-depth insight into the molecular mechanisms of a particular organism. In particular, these models correlate the&nbsp;<a title="Genome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome">genome</a>&nbsp;with molecular&nbsp;<a title="Physiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiology">physiology</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Metaheuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaheuristic">Metaheuristic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization">mathematical optimization</a>, a metaheuristic is a higher-level&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Procedure (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedure_(computer_science)">procedure</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Heuristic (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heuristic_(computer_science)">heuristic</a>&nbsp;designed to find, generate, or select a heuristic (partial&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search algorithm</a>) that may provide a sufficiently good solution to an&nbsp;<a title="Optimization problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_problem">optimization problem</a>, especially with incomplete or imperfect information or limited computation capacity.&nbsp;Metaheuristics sample a set of solutions which is too large to be completely sampled.</li>
<li><a title="Model checking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_checking">Model checking</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, model checking or property checking is, for a given model of a system, exhaustively and automatically checking whether this model meets a given&nbsp;<a title="Formal specification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_specification">specification</a>. Typically, one has hardware or software systems in mind, whereas the specification contains safety requirements such as the absence of&nbsp;<a title="Deadlock" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deadlock">deadlocks</a>&nbsp;and similar critical states that can cause the system to&nbsp;<a title="Crash (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crash_(computing)">crash</a>. Model checking is a technique for automatically verifying correctness properties of&nbsp;<em>finite-state</em>&nbsp;systems.</li>
<li><a title="Modus ponens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modus_ponens">Modus ponens</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Propositional calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_calculus">propositional logic</a>,&nbsp;<em>modus ponens</em>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Rule of inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_inference">rule of inference</a>.&nbsp;It can be summarized as "<em>P&nbsp;<a title="Material conditional" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Material_conditional">implies</a>&nbsp;Q</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>P</em>&nbsp;is asserted to be true, therefore&nbsp;<em>Q</em>&nbsp;must be true."</li>
<li><a title="Modus tollens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modus_tollens">Modus tollens</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Propositional calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_calculus">propositional logic</a>,&nbsp;<em>modus tollens</em>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Validity (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Validity_(logic)">valid</a>&nbsp;<a title="Logical form" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_form">argument form</a>&nbsp;and a&nbsp;<a title="Rule of inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_inference">rule of inference</a>. It is an application of the general truth that if a statement is true, then so is its&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Contrapositive" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contrapositive">contrapositive</a>. The inference rule&nbsp;<em>modus tollens</em>&nbsp;asserts that the&nbsp;<a title="Inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference">inference</a>&nbsp;from&nbsp;<em>P implies Q</em>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<em>the negation of Q implies the negation of P</em>&nbsp;is valid.</li>
<li><a title="Monte Carlo tree search" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monte_Carlo_tree_search">Monte Carlo tree search</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, Monte Carlo tree search (MCTS) is a&nbsp;<a title="Heuristic (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heuristic_(computer_science)">heuristic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search algorithm</a>&nbsp;for some kinds of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Decision process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_process">decision processes</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Multi-agent system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-agent_system">Multi-agent system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (MAS or "self-organized system"), is a computerized system composed of multiple interacting&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>. Multi-agent systems can solve problems that are difficult or impossible for an individual agent or a&nbsp;<a title="Monolithic system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monolithic_system">monolithic system</a>&nbsp;to solve. Intelligence may include&nbsp;<a title="Scientific method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_method">methodic</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Function (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(computer_science)">functional</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">procedural</a>&nbsp;approaches,&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithmic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Multi-swarm optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-swarm_optimization">Multi-swarm optimization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a variant of&nbsp;<a title="Particle swarm optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Particle_swarm_optimization">particle swarm optimization</a>&nbsp;(PSO) based on the use of multiple sub-swarms instead of one (standard) swarm. The general approach in multi-swarm optimization is that each sub-swarm focuses on a specific region while a specific diversification method decides where and when to launch the sub-swarms. The multi-swarm framework is especially fitted for the optimization on multi-modal problems, where multiple (local) optima exist.</li>
<li><a title="Mutation (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation_(genetic_algorithm)">Mutation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Genetic operator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_operator">genetic operator</a>&nbsp;used to maintain&nbsp;<a title="Genetic diversity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_diversity">genetic diversity</a>&nbsp;from one generation of a population of&nbsp;<a title="Genetic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithm">genetic algorithm</a>&nbsp;<a title="Chromosome (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome_(genetic_algorithm)">chromosomes</a>&nbsp;to the next. It is analogous to biological&nbsp;<a title="Mutation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation">mutation</a>. Mutation alters one or more gene values in a chromosome from its initial state. In mutation, the solution may change entirely from the previous solution. Hence GA can come to a better solution by using mutation. Mutation occurs during evolution according to a user-definable mutation probability. This probability should be set low. If it is set too high, the search will turn into a primitive random search.</li>
<li><a title="Mycin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mycin">Mycin</a>&nbsp;&ndash; was an early&nbsp;<a title="Backward chaining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backward_chaining">backward chaining</a>&nbsp;<a title="Expert system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_system">expert system</a>&nbsp;that used&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;to identify bacteria causing severe infections, such as&nbsp;<a title="Bacteremia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteremia">bacteremia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Meningitis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meningitis">meningitis</a>, and to recommend&nbsp;<a title="Antibiotic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antibiotic">antibiotics</a>, with the dosage adjusted for patient's body weight &ndash; the name derived from the antibiotics themselves, as many antibiotics have the suffix "-mycin". The MYCIN system was also used for the diagnosis of blood clotting diseases.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="N" class="mw-headline">N</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Naive Bayes classifier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naive_Bayes_classifier">Naive Bayes classifier</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, naive Bayes classifiers are a family of simple&nbsp;<a title="Probabilistic classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilistic_classification">probabilistic classifiers</a>&nbsp;based on applying&nbsp;<a title="Bayes' theorem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayes%27_theorem">Bayes' theorem</a>&nbsp;with strong (naive)&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical independence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_independence">independence</a>&nbsp;assumptions between the features.</li>
<li><a title="Naive semantics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naive_semantics">Naive semantics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an approach used in computer science for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">representing basic knowledge</a>&nbsp;about a specific domain, and has been used in applications such as the representation of the meaning of natural language sentences in artificial intelligence applications. In a general setting the term has been used to refer to the use of a limited store of generally understood knowledge about a specific domain in the world, and has been applied to fields such as the knowledge based design of data schemas.</li>
<li><a title="Name binding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_binding">Name binding</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In programming languages, name binding is the association of entities (data and/or code) with&nbsp;<a title="Identifier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identifier">identifiers</a>.&nbsp;An identifier bound to an object is said to&nbsp;<a title="Reference (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_(computer_science)">reference</a>&nbsp;that object.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Machine language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_language">Machine languages</a>&nbsp;have no built-in notion of identifiers, but name-object bindings as a service and notation for the programmer is implemented by programming languages. Binding is intimately connected with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Scoping" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scoping">scoping</a>, as scope determines which names bind to which objects &ndash; at which locations in the program code (<a title="Scope (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scope_(computer_science)#Lexical_scoping">lexically</a>) and in which one of the possible execution paths (<a title="Scope (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scope_(computer_science)#Dynamic_scoping">temporally</a>). Use of an identifier&nbsp;<code>id</code>&nbsp;in a context that establishes a binding for&nbsp;<code>id</code>&nbsp;is called a binding (or defining) occurrence. In all other occurrences (e.g., in expressions, assignments, and subprogram calls), an identifier stands for what it is bound to; such occurrences are called applied occurrences.</li>
<li><a title="Named-entity recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Named-entity_recognition">Named-entity recognition</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (NER), (also known as entity identification, entity chunking and entity extraction) is a subtask of&nbsp;<a title="Information extraction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_extraction">information extraction</a>&nbsp;that seeks to locate and classify&nbsp;<a title="Named entity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Named_entity">named entity</a>&nbsp;mentions in&nbsp;<a title="Unstructured data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unstructured_data">unstructured text</a>&nbsp;into pre-defined categories such as the person names, organizations, locations,&nbsp;<a title="Medical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_classification">medical codes</a>, time expressions, quantities, monetary values, percentages, etc.</li>
<li><a title="Named graph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Named_graph">Named graph</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Named graphs are a key concept of&nbsp;<a title="Semantic Web" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_Web">Semantic Web</a>&nbsp;architecture in which a set of&nbsp;<a title="Resource Description Framework" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework">Resource Description Framework</a>&nbsp;statements (a&nbsp;<a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">graph</a>) are identified using a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="URI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/URI">URI</a>, allowing descriptions to be made of that set of statements such as context, provenance information or other such&nbsp;<a title="Metadata" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metadata">metadata</a>. Named graphs are a simple extension of the RDF data model&nbsp;through which graphs can be created but the model lacks an effective means of distinguishing between them once published on the&nbsp;<a title="World Wide Web" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web">Web</a>&nbsp;at large.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language generation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_generation">Natural language generation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (NLG), is a software process that transforms structured data into plain-English content. It can be used to produce long-form content for organizations to automate custom reports, as well as produce custom content for a web or mobile application. It can also be used to generate short blurbs of text in interactive conversations (a&nbsp;<a title="Chatbot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chatbot">chatbot</a>) which might even be read out loud by a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Text-to-speech" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Text-to-speech">text-to-speech</a>&nbsp;system.</li>
<li><a title="Natural language processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing">Natural language processing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (NLP), is a subfield of computer science, information engineering, and artificial intelligence concerned with the interactions between computers and human (natural) languages, in particular how to program computers to process and analyze large amounts of&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural language</a>&nbsp;data.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_programming">Natural language programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Ontology (information science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_(information_science)">ontology</a>-assisted way of&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming</a>&nbsp;in terms of&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural-language</a>&nbsp;sentences, e.g.&nbsp;<a title="English language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language">English</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Network motif" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_motif">Network motif</a>&nbsp;&ndash; All networks, including biological networks, social networks, technological networks (e.g., computer networks and electrical circuits) and more, can be represented as&nbsp;<a title="Complex network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_network">graphs</a>, which include a wide variety of subgraphs. One important local property of networks are so-called network motifs, which are defined as recurrent and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statistically significant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistically_significant">statistically significant</a>&nbsp;sub-graphs or patterns.</li>
<li><a title="Neural machine translation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_machine_translation">Neural machine translation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (NMT), is an approach to&nbsp;<a title="Machine translation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_translation">machine translation</a>&nbsp;that uses a large&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;to predict the likelihood of a sequence of words, typically modeling entire sentences in a single integrated model.</li>
<li><a title="Neural Turing machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_Turing_machine">Neural Turing machine</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (NTMs) is a&nbsp;<a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network">recurrent neural network</a>&nbsp;model. NTMs combine the fuzzy&nbsp;<a title="Pattern matching" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_matching">pattern matching</a>&nbsp;capabilities of&nbsp;<a title="Neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network">neural networks</a>&nbsp;with the&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithmic</a>&nbsp;power of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Programmable computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmable_computer">programmable computers</a>. An NTM has a neural network controller coupled to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliary memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auxiliary_memory">external memory</a>&nbsp;resources, which it interacts with through attentional mechanisms. The memory interactions are differentiable end-to-end, making it possible to optimize them using&nbsp;<a title="Gradient descent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient_descent">gradient descent</a>.&nbsp;An NTM with a&nbsp;<a title="Long short-term memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_short-term_memory">long short-term memory</a>&nbsp;(LSTM) network controller can infer simple algorithms such as copying, sorting, and associative recall from examples alone.</li>
<li><a title="Neuro-fuzzy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuro-fuzzy">Neuro-fuzzy</a>&nbsp;&ndash; refers to combinations of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Fuzzy logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_logic">fuzzy logic</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Neurocybernetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurocybernetics">Neurocybernetics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; A brain&ndash;computer interface (BCI), sometimes called a neural-control interface (NCI), mind-machine interface (MMI), direct neural interface (DNI), or brain&ndash;machine interface (BMI), is a direct communication pathway between an enhanced or wired&nbsp;<a title="Brain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain">brain</a>&nbsp;and an external device. BCI differs from&nbsp;<a title="Neuromodulation (medicine)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuromodulation_(medicine)">neuromodulation</a>&nbsp;in that it allows for bidirectional information flow. BCIs are often directed at researching, mapping, assisting, augmenting, or repairing human cognitive or sensory-motor functions.</li>
<li><a title="Neuromorphic engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuromorphic_engineering">Neuromorphic engineering</a>&nbsp;&ndash; also known as neuromorphic computing,&nbsp;is a concept describing the use of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Very-large-scale integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Very-large-scale_integration">very-large-scale integration</a>&nbsp;(VLSI) systems containing electronic&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Analog circuit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analog_circuit">analog circuits</a>&nbsp;to mimic neuro-biological architectures present in the nervous system.&nbsp;In recent times, the term&nbsp;<em>neuromorphic</em>&nbsp;has been used to describe analog, digital, mixed-mode analog/digital VLSI, and software systems that implement models of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Neural system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_system">neural systems</a>&nbsp;(for&nbsp;<a title="Perception" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perception">perception</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Motor control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motor_control">motor control</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Multisensory integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multisensory_integration">multisensory integration</a>). The implementation of neuromorphic computing on the hardware level can be realized by oxide-based&nbsp;<a title="Memristor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memristor">memristors</a>,&nbsp;spintronic memories,&nbsp;threshold switches, and&nbsp;<a title="Transistor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transistor">transistors</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Node (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(computer_science)">Node</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a basic unit of a&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>, such as a&nbsp;<a title="Linked list" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linked_list">linked list</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Tree (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_(data_structure)">tree</a>&nbsp;data structure. Nodes contain&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>&nbsp;and also may link to other nodes. Links between nodes are often implemented by&nbsp;<a title="Pointer (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pointer_(computer_programming)">pointers</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Nondeterministic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nondeterministic_algorithm">Nondeterministic algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;that, even for the same input, can exhibit different behaviors on different runs, as opposed to a&nbsp;<a title="Deterministic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deterministic_algorithm">deterministic algorithm</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Nouvelle AI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nouvelle_AI">Nouvelle AI</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Nouvelle AI differs from classical AI by aiming to produce robots with intelligence levels similar to insects. Researchers believe that intelligence can emerge organically from simple behaviors as these intelligences interacted with the "real world," instead of using the constructed worlds which symbolic AIs typically needed to have programmed into them.</li>
<li><a title="NP (complexity)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NP_(complexity)">NP</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">computational complexity theory</a>, NP (nondeterministic polynomial time) is a&nbsp;<a title="Complexity class" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complexity_class">complexity class</a>&nbsp;used to classify&nbsp;<a title="Decision problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_problem">decision problems</a>. NP is the&nbsp;<a title="Set (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_(mathematics)">set</a>&nbsp;of decision problems for which the&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory#Problem_instances">problem instances</a>, where the answer is "yes", have&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical proof" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_proof">proofs</a>&nbsp;verifiable in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Polynomial time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynomial_time">polynomial time</a>.</li>
<li><a title="NP-completeness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NP-completeness">NP-completeness</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">computational complexity theory</a>, a problem is NP-complete when it can be solved by a restricted class of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Brute force search" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brute_force_search">brute force search</a>&nbsp;algorithms and it can be used to simulate any other problem with a similar algorithm. More precisely, each input to the problem should be associated with a set of solutions of polynomial length, whose validity can be tested quickly (in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Polynomial time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynomial_time">polynomial time</a>), such that the output for any input is "yes" if the solution set is non-empty and "no" if it is empty.</li>
<li><a title="NP-hardness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NP-hardness">NP-hardness</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (<a title="NP (complexity)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NP_(complexity)">non-deterministic polynomial-time</a>&nbsp;hardness), in&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">computational complexity theory</a>, is the defining property of a class of problems that are, informally, "at least as hard as the hardest problems in NP". A simple example of an NP-hard problem is the&nbsp;<a title="Subset sum problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subset_sum_problem">subset sum problem</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="O" class="mw-headline">O</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Occam's razor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occam%27s_razor">Occam's razor</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also Ockham's razor or Ocham's razor), is the problem-solving&nbsp;<a title="Principle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principle">principle</a>&nbsp;that states that when presented with competing&nbsp;<a title="Hypothesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothesis">hypotheses</a>&nbsp;that make the same predictions, one should select the solution with the fewest assumptions&nbsp;and is not meant to filter out hypotheses that make different predictions. The idea is attributed to English&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franciscan">Franciscan</a>&nbsp;friar&nbsp;<a title="William of Ockham" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_of_Ockham">William of Ockham</a>&nbsp;(<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr>&nbsp;1287&ndash;1347), a&nbsp;<a title="Scholasticism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholasticism">scholastic</a>&nbsp;philosopher and&nbsp;<a title="Catholic theology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_theology">theologian</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Offline learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Offline_learning">Offline learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><a title="Online machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Online_machine_learning">Online machine learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a method of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;in which data becomes available in a sequential order and is used to update the best predictor for future data at each step, as opposed to batch learning techniques which generate the best predictor by learning on the entire training data set at once. Online learning is a common technique used in areas of machine learning where it is computationally infeasible to train over the entire dataset, requiring the need of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Out-of-core" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Out-of-core">out-of-core</a>&nbsp;algorithms. It is also used in situations where it is necessary for the algorithm to dynamically adapt to new patterns in the data, or when the data itself is generated as a function of time.</li>
<li><a title="Ontology learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_learning">Ontology learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (ontology extraction, ontology generation, or ontology acquisition), is the automatic or semi-automatic creation of&nbsp;<a title="Ontology (information science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_(information_science)">ontologies</a>, including extracting the corresponding&nbsp;<a title="Domain of discourse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_of_discourse">domain's</a>&nbsp;terms and the relationships between the&nbsp;<a title="Conceptualization (information science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conceptualization_(information_science)">concepts</a>&nbsp;that these terms represent from a&nbsp;<a title="Text corpus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Text_corpus">corpus</a>&nbsp;of natural language text, and encoding them with an&nbsp;<a title="Ontology language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_language">ontology language</a>&nbsp;for easy retrieval.</li>
<li><a title="OpenAI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenAI">OpenAI</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the for-profit corporation OpenAI LP, whose&nbsp;<a title="Parent company" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parent_company">parent organization</a>&nbsp;is the non-profit organization OpenAI Inc&nbsp;that conducts research in the field of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;(AI) with the stated aim to promote and develop&nbsp;<a title="Friendly artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friendly_artificial_intelligence">friendly AI</a>&nbsp;in such a way as to benefit humanity as a whole.</li>
<li><a title="OpenCog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenCog">OpenCog</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a project that aims to build an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Open source software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_source_software">open source</a>&nbsp;artificial intelligence framework. OpenCog Prime is an architecture for robot and virtual&nbsp;<a title="Embodied cognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embodied_cognition">embodied cognition</a>&nbsp;that defines a set of interacting components designed to give rise to human-equivalent&nbsp;<a title="Artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence">artificial general intelligence</a>&nbsp;(AGI) as an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Emergent phenomenon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergent_phenomenon">emergent phenomenon</a>&nbsp;of the whole system.</li>
<li><a title="Open Mind Common Sense" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_Mind_Common_Sense">Open Mind Common Sense</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an artificial intelligence project based at the&nbsp;<a title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>&nbsp;(MIT)&nbsp;<a title="MIT Media Lab" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT_Media_Lab">Media Lab</a>&nbsp;whose goal is to build and utilize a large&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Commonsense knowledge base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_knowledge_base">commonsense knowledge base</a>&nbsp;from the contributions of many thousands of people across the Web.</li>
<li><a title="Open-source software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_software">Open-source software</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (OSS), is a type of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_software">computer software</a>&nbsp;in which&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;is released under a&nbsp;<a title="Open-source license" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_license">license</a>&nbsp;in which the&nbsp;<a title="Copyright" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright">copyright</a>&nbsp;holder grants users the rights to study, change, and&nbsp;<a title="Software distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_distribution">distribute the software</a>&nbsp;to anyone and for any purpose.&nbsp;Open-source&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;may be developed in a&nbsp;<a title="Open-source model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_model">collaborative public manner</a>. Open-source software is a prominent example of&nbsp;<a title="Open collaboration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_collaboration">open collaboration</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="P" class="mw-headline">P</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Partial order reduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partial_order_reduction">Partial order reduction</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a technique for reducing the size of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="State transition system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_transition_system">state-space</a>&nbsp;to be searched by a&nbsp;<a title="Model checking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_checking">model checking</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Automated planning and scheduling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning_and_scheduling">automated planning and scheduling</a>&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>. It exploits the commutativity of concurrently executed&nbsp;<a title="Transition (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transition_(computer_science)">transitions</a>, which result in the same state when executed in different orders.</li>
<li><a title="Partially observable Markov decision process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partially_observable_Markov_decision_process">Partially observable Markov decision process</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (POMDP), is a generalization of a&nbsp;<a title="Markov decision process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_decision_process">Markov decision process</a>&nbsp;(MDP). A POMDP models an agent decision process in which it is assumed that the system dynamics are determined by an MDP, but the agent cannot directly observe the underlying state. Instead, it must maintain a probability distribution over the set of possible states, based on a set of observations and observation probabilities, and the underlying MDP.</li>
<li><a title="Particle swarm optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Particle_swarm_optimization">Particle swarm optimization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (PSO) is a computational method that&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization">optimizes</a>&nbsp;a problem by&nbsp;<a title="Iterative method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iterative_method">iteratively</a>&nbsp;trying to improve a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Candidate solution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Candidate_solution">candidate solution</a>&nbsp;with regard to a given measure of quality. It solves a problem by having a population of candidate solutions, here dubbed&nbsp;<a title="Point particle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_particle">particles</a>, and moving these particles around in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Optimization (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_(mathematics)#Concepts_and_notation">search-space</a>&nbsp;according to simple&nbsp;<a title="Formula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formula">mathematical formulae</a>&nbsp;over the particle's&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Position (vector)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Position_(vector)">position</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Velocity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Velocity">velocity</a>. Each particle's movement is influenced by its local best known position, but is also guided toward the best known positions in the search-space, which are updated as better positions are found by other particles. This is expected to move the swarm toward the best solutions.</li>
<li><a title="Pathfinding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pathfinding">Pathfinding</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or pathing, is the plotting, by a computer application, of the shortest route between two points. It is a more practical variant on&nbsp;<a title="Maze" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maze#Solving_mazes">solving mazes</a>. This field of research is based heavily on&nbsp;<a title="Dijkstra's algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dijkstra%27s_algorithm">Dijkstra's algorithm</a>&nbsp;for finding a shortest path on a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_graph_theory#Weighted_graphs_and_networks">weighted graph</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Pattern recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_recognition">Pattern recognition</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is concerned with the automatic discovery of regularities in data through the use of computer algorithms and with the use of these regularities to take actions such as classifying the data into different categories.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Predicate logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predicate_logic">Predicate logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; First-order logic&mdash;also known as predicate logic and first-order predicate calculus&mdash;is a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Formal system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_system">formal systems</a>&nbsp;used in&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Philosophy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">philosophy</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>. First-order logic uses&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Quantification (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantification_(logic)">quantified variables</a>&nbsp;over non-logical objects and allows the use of sentences that contain variables, so that rather than propositions such as&nbsp;<em>Socrates is a man</em>&nbsp;one can have expressions in the form "there exists x such that x is Socrates and x is a man" and&nbsp;<em>there exists</em>&nbsp;is a quantifier while&nbsp;<em>x</em>&nbsp;is a variable.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_174-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_artificial_intelligence#cite_note-auto-174">[174]</a></sup>&nbsp;This distinguishes it from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Propositional logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_logic">propositional logic</a>, which does not use quantifiers or&nbsp;<a title="Finitary relation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finitary_relation">relations</a>;&nbsp;in this sense, propositional logic is the foundation of first-order logic.</li>
<li><a title="Predictive analytics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predictive_analytics">Predictive analytics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; encompasses a variety of statistical techniques from&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data mining</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Predictive modelling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predictive_modelling">predictive modelling</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, that analyze current and historical facts to make predictions about future or otherwise unknown events.</li>
<li><a title="Principal component analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principal_component_analysis">Principal component analysis</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (PCA), is a statistical procedure that uses an&nbsp;<a title="Orthogonal transformation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthogonal_transformation">orthogonal transformation</a>&nbsp;to convert a set of observations of possibly correlated variables (entities each of which takes on various numerical values) into a set of values of&nbsp;<a title="Correlation and dependence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Correlation_and_dependence">linearly uncorrelated</a>&nbsp;variables called principal components. This transformation is defined in such a way that the first principal component has the largest possible&nbsp;<a title="Variance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variance">variance</a>&nbsp;(that is, accounts for as much of the variability in the data as possible), and each succeeding component, in turn, has the highest variance possible under the constraint that it is&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orthogonal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthogonal">orthogonal</a>&nbsp;to the preceding components. The resulting vectors (each being a&nbsp;<a title="Linear combination" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_combination">linear combination</a>&nbsp;of the variables and containing&nbsp;<em>n</em>&nbsp;observations) are an uncorrelated&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orthogonal basis set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthogonal_basis_set">orthogonal basis set</a>. PCA is sensitive to the relative scaling of the original variables.</li>
<li><a title="Principle of rationality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principle_of_rationality">Principle of rationality</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (or rationality principle), was coined by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Karl R. Popper" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_R._Popper">Karl R. Popper</a>&nbsp;in his Harvard Lecture of 1963, and published in his book&nbsp;<em>Myth of Framework</em>.&nbsp;It is related to what he called the 'logic of the situation' in an&nbsp;<em>Economica</em>&nbsp;article of 1944/1945, published later in his book&nbsp;<em>The Poverty of Historicism</em>.&nbsp;According to Popper's rationality principle, agents act in the most adequate way according to the objective situation. It is an idealized conception of human behavior which he used to drive his model of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Situational analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Situational_analysis">situational analysis</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Probabilistic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilistic_programming">Probabilistic programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (PP), is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;in which&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Probabilistic model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilistic_model">probabilistic models</a>&nbsp;are specified and inference for these models is performed automatically.&nbsp;It represents an attempt to unify probabilistic modeling and traditional general-purpose programming in order to make the former easier and more widely applicable.&nbsp;It can be used to create systems that help make decisions in the face of uncertainty. Programming languages used for probabilistic programming are referred to as "Probabilistic programming languages" (PPLs).</li>
<li><a title="Production system (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Production_system_(computer_science)">Production system</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;is a computer program typically used to provide some form of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, which consists primarily of a set of rules about behavior but it also includes the mechanism necessary to follow those rules as the system responds to states of the world.</li>
<li><a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">Programming language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Formal language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_language">formal language</a>, which comprises a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Instruction set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_set">set of instructions</a>&nbsp;that produce various kinds of&nbsp;<a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output">output</a>. Programming languages are used in&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>&nbsp;to implement&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Prolog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prolog">Prolog</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">logic programming</a>&nbsp;language associated with artificial intelligence and&nbsp;<a title="Computational linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_linguistics">computational linguistics</a>. Prolog has its roots in&nbsp;<a title="First-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_logic">first-order logic</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_logic">formal logic</a>, and unlike many other&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming languages</a>, Prolog is intended primarily as a&nbsp;<a title="Declarative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declarative_programming">declarative</a>&nbsp;programming language: the program logic is expressed in terms of relations, represented as facts and&nbsp;<a title="Rule of inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_inference">rules</a>. A computation is initiated by running a&nbsp;<em>query</em>&nbsp;over these relations.</li>
<li><a title="Propositional calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_calculus">Propositional calculus</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>. It is also called propositional logic, statement logic, sentential calculus, sentential logic, or sometimes&nbsp;<strong><a title="Zeroth-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeroth-order_logic">zeroth-order logic</a></strong>. It deals with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Propositions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositions">propositions</a>&nbsp;(which can be true or false) and argument flow. Compound propositions are formed by connecting propositions by&nbsp;<a title="Logical connective" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_connective">logical connectives</a>. The propositions without logical connectives are called atomic propositions. Unlike&nbsp;<a title="First-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_logic">first-order logic</a>, propositional logic does not deal with non-logical objects, predicates about them, or quantifiers. However, all the machinery of propositional logic is included in first-order logic and higher-order logics. In this sense, propositional logic is the foundation of first-order logic and higher-order logic.</li>
<li><a title="Python (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Python_(programming_language)">Python</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Interpreted language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpreted_language">interpreted</a>,&nbsp;<a title="High-level programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-level_programming_language">high-level</a>,&nbsp;<a title="General-purpose programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General-purpose_programming_language">general-purpose</a>&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>. Created by&nbsp;<a title="Guido van Rossum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guido_van_Rossum">Guido van Rossum</a>&nbsp;and first released in 1991, Python's design philosophy emphasizes&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Code readability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_readability">code readability</a>&nbsp;with its notable use of&nbsp;<a title="Off-side rule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Off-side_rule">significant whitespace</a>. Its language constructs and&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented</a>&nbsp;approach aim to help programmers write clear, logical code for small and large-scale projects.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Q" class="mw-headline">Q</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Qualification problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qualification_problem">Qualification problem</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In philosophy and artificial intelligence (especially,&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge-based systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge-based_systems">knowledge-based systems</a>), the qualification problem is concerned with the impossibility of listing&nbsp;<em>all</em>&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a title="Precondition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precondition">preconditions</a>&nbsp;required for a real-world action to have its intended effect.&nbsp;It might be posed as&nbsp;<em>how to deal with the things that prevent me from achieving my intended result</em>. It is strongly connected to, and opposite the&nbsp;<a title="Ramification problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramification_problem">ramification side</a>&nbsp;of, the&nbsp;<a title="Frame problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame_problem">frame problem</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Quantifier (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantifier_(logic)">Quantifier</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>, quantification specifies the quantity of specimens in the&nbsp;<a title="Domain of discourse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_of_discourse">domain of discourse</a>&nbsp;that satisfy an&nbsp;<a title="Open formula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_formula">open formula</a>. The two most common quantifiers mean "<a title="Universal quantification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_quantification">for all</a>" and "<a title="Existential quantification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existential_quantification">there exists</a>". For example, in arithmetic, quantifiers allow one to say that the natural numbers go on forever, by writing that&nbsp;<em>for all</em>&nbsp;n (where n is a natural number), there is another number (say, the successor of n) which is one bigger than n.</li>
<li><a title="Quantum computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computing">Quantum computing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the use of&nbsp;<a title="Quantum mechanics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics">quantum-mechanical</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Phenomena" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenomena">phenomena</a>&nbsp;such as&nbsp;<a title="Quantum superposition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_superposition">superposition</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Quantum entanglement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_entanglement">entanglement</a>&nbsp;to perform&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>. A quantum computer is used to perform such computation, which can be implemented theoretically or physically.</li>
<li><a title="Query language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Query_language">Query language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Query languages or data query languages (DQLs) are&nbsp;<a title="Computer language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_language">computer languages</a>&nbsp;used to make queries in&nbsp;<a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database">databases</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Information system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_system">information systems</a>. Broadly, query languages can be classified according to whether they are database query languages or&nbsp;<a title="Information retrieval query language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_retrieval_query_language">information retrieval query languages</a>. The difference is that a database query language attempts to give factual answers to factual questions, while an information retrieval query language attempts to find documents containing information that is relevant to an area of inquiry.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="R" class="mw-headline">R</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="R (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R_(programming_language)">R programming language</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Free software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_software">free software</a>&nbsp;environment for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_computing">statistical computing</a>&nbsp;and graphics supported by the R Foundation for Statistical Computing.&nbsp;The R language is widely used among&nbsp;<a title="Statistician" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistician">statisticians</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data miners</a>&nbsp;for developing&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_software">statistical software</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Data analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_analysis">data analysis</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Radial basis function network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radial_basis_function_network">Radial basis function network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In the field of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematical modeling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_modeling">mathematical modeling</a>, a radial basis function network is an&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;that uses&nbsp;<a title="Radial basis function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radial_basis_function">radial basis functions</a>&nbsp;as&nbsp;<a title="Activation function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activation_function">activation functions</a>. The output of the network is a&nbsp;<a title="Linear combination" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_combination">linear combination</a>&nbsp;of radial basis functions of the inputs and neuron parameters. Radial basis function networks have many uses, including&nbsp;<a title="Function approximation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_approximation">function approximation</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Time series prediction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_series_prediction">time series prediction</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">classification</a>, and system&nbsp;<a title="Control theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_theory">control</a>. They were first formulated in a 1988 paper by Broomhead and Lowe, both researchers at the&nbsp;<a title="Royal Signals and Radar Establishment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Signals_and_Radar_Establishment">Royal Signals and Radar Establishment</a>.</li>
