<li><a title="Random forest" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_forest">Random forest</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Random forests, or random decision forests, are an&nbsp;<a title="Ensemble learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ensemble_learning">ensemble learning</a>&nbsp;method for&nbsp;<a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">classification</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Regression analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regression_analysis">regression</a>&nbsp;and other tasks that operates by constructing a multitude of&nbsp;<a title="Decision tree learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_tree_learning">decision trees</a>&nbsp;at training time and outputting the class that is the&nbsp;<a title="Mode (statistics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mode_(statistics)">mode</a>&nbsp;of the classes (classification) or mean prediction (regression) of the individual trees.&nbsp;Random decision forests correct for decision trees' habit of&nbsp;<a title="Overfitting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overfitting">overfitting</a>&nbsp;to their&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Test set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Test_set">training set</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Reasoning system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning_system">Reasoning system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Information technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_technology">information technology</a>&nbsp;a reasoning system is a&nbsp;<a title="Software system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_system">software system</a>&nbsp;that generates conclusions from available&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge">knowledge</a>&nbsp;using&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logical</a>&nbsp;techniques such as&nbsp;<a title="Deductive reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deductive_reasoning">deduction</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Inductive reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inductive_reasoning">induction</a>. Reasoning systems play an important role in the implementation of artificial intelligence and&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge-based systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge-based_systems">knowledge-based systems</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Recurrent neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network">Recurrent neural network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (RNN), is a class of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;where connections between nodes form a&nbsp;<a title="Directed graph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directed_graph">directed graph</a>&nbsp;along a temporal sequence. This allows it to exhibit temporal dynamic behavior. Unlike&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Feedforward neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feedforward_neural_networks">feedforward neural networks</a>, RNNs can use their internal state (memory) to process sequences of inputs. This makes them applicable to tasks such as unsegmented, connected&nbsp;<a title="Handwriting recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Handwriting_recognition">handwriting recognition</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Speech recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_recognition">speech recognition</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Region connection calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Region_connection_calculus">Region connection calculus</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>RCC</strong>), is intended to serve for qualitative spatial representation and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Spatial-temporal reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spatial-temporal_reasoning">reasoning</a>. RCC abstractly describes regions (in&nbsp;<a title="Euclidean space" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euclidean_space">Euclidean space</a>, or in a&nbsp;<a title="Topological space" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topological_space">topological space</a>) by their possible relations to each other.</li>
<li><a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">Reinforcement learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (RL), is an area of&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;concerned with how&nbsp;<a title="Software agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_agent">software agents</a>&nbsp;ought to take&nbsp;<a title="Action selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Action_selection">actions</a>&nbsp;in an environment so as to maximize some notion of cumulative reward. Reinforcement learning is one of three basic machine learning paradigms, alongside&nbsp;<a title="Supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning">supervised learning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Unsupervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unsupervised_learning">unsupervised learning</a>. It differs from supervised learning in that labelled input/output pairs need not be presented, and sub-optimal actions need not be explicitly corrected. Instead the focus is finding a balance between exploration (of uncharted territory) and exploitation (of current knowledge).</li>
<li><a title="Reservoir computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reservoir_computing">Reservoir computing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a framework for computation that may be viewed as an extension of&nbsp;<a title="Neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network">neural networks</a>.&nbsp;Typically an input signal is fed into a fixed (random)&nbsp;<a title="Dynamical system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamical_system">dynamical system</a>&nbsp;called a&nbsp;<em>reservoir</em>&nbsp;and the dynamics of the reservoir map the input to a higher dimension. Then a simple&nbsp;<em>readout</em>&nbsp;mechanism is trained to read the state of the reservoir and map it to the desired output. The main benefit is that training is performed only at the readout stage and the reservoir is fixed.&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid-state machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquid-state_machine">Liquid-state machines</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Echo state network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Echo_state_network">echo state networks</a>&nbsp;are two major types of reservoir computing.</li>
<li><a title="Resource Description Framework" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework">Resource Description Framework</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <strong>(RDF)</strong>, is a family of&nbsp;<a title="World Wide Web Consortium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium</a>&nbsp;(W3C)&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Specification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Specification">specifications</a>&nbsp;originally designed as a&nbsp;<a title="Metadata" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metadata">metadata</a>&nbsp;<a title="Data model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_model">data model</a>. It has come to be used as a general method for conceptual description or modeling of information that is implemented in&nbsp;<a title="Web resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_resource">web resources</a>, using a variety of syntax notations and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Data serialization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_serialization">data serialization</a>&nbsp;formats. It is also used in&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge management" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_management">knowledge management</a>&nbsp;applications.</li>
<li><a title="Restricted Boltzmann machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restricted_Boltzmann_machine">Restricted Boltzmann machine</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (RBM), is a&nbsp;<a title="Generative model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_model">generative</a>&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_neural_network">stochastic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;that can learn a&nbsp;<a title="Probability distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_distribution">probability distribution</a>&nbsp;over its set of inputs.</li>
<li><a title="Rete algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rete_algorithm">Rete algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Pattern matching" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_matching">pattern matching</a>&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;for implementing&nbsp;<a title="Rule-based system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule-based_system">rule-based systems</a>. The algorithm was developed to efficiently apply many&nbsp;<a title="Rule of inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_inference">rules</a>&nbsp;or patterns to many objects, or&nbsp;<a title="Fact" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fact">facts</a>, in a&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_base">knowledge base</a>. It is used to determine which of the system's rules should fire based on its data store, its facts.</li>
<li><a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">Robotics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Interdisciplinarity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;branch of&nbsp;<a title="List of engineering branches" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_engineering_branches">engineering</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Branch of science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branch_of_science">science</a>&nbsp;that includes&nbsp;<a title="Mechanical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanical_engineering">mechanical engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Electronic engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_engineering">electronic engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information engineering (field)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_engineering_(field)">information engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, and others. Robotics deals with the design, construction, operation, and use of&nbsp;<a title="Robot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot">robots</a>, as well as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_system">computer systems</a>&nbsp;for their control,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sensory feedback" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensory_feedback">sensory feedback</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Information processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_processing">information processing</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Rule-based system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule-based_system">Rule-based system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, a rule-based system is used to store and manipulate knowledge to interpret information in a useful way. It is often used in artificial intelligence applications and research. Normally, the term&nbsp;<em>rule-based system</em>&nbsp;is applied to systems involving human-crafted or curated rule sets. Rule-based systems constructed using automatic rule inference, such as&nbsp;<a title="Rule-based machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule-based_machine_learning">rule-based machine learning</a>, are normally excluded from this system type.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="S" class="mw-headline">S</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Satisfiability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satisfiability">Satisfiability</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">mathematical logic</a>, satisfiability and&nbsp;<a title="Validity (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Validity_(logic)">validity</a>&nbsp;are elementary concepts of&nbsp;<a title="Semantics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantics">semantics</a>. A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formula (mathematical logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formula_(mathematical_logic)">formula</a>&nbsp;is&nbsp;<em>satisfiable</em>&nbsp;if it is possible to find an&nbsp;<a title="Interpretation (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpretation_(logic)">interpretation</a>&nbsp;(<a title="Model theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_theory">model</a>) that makes the formula true.&nbsp;A formula is&nbsp;<em>valid</em>&nbsp;if all interpretations make the formula true. The opposites of these concepts are unsatisfiability and invalidity, that is, a formula is&nbsp;<em>unsatisfiable</em>&nbsp;if none of the interpretations make the formula true, and&nbsp;<em>invalid</em>&nbsp;if some such interpretation makes the formula false. These four concepts are related to each other in a manner exactly analogous to&nbsp;<a title="Aristotle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle">Aristotle</a>'s&nbsp;<a title="Square of opposition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Square_of_opposition">square of opposition</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">Search algorithm</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is any&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;which solves the&nbsp;<a title="Search problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_problem">search problem</a>, namely, to retrieve information stored within some data structure, or calculated in the&nbsp;<a title="Feasible region" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feasible_region">search space</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Problem domain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Problem_domain">problem domain</a>, either with&nbsp;<a title="Continuous or discrete variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuous_or_discrete_variable">discrete or continuous values</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Selection (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selection_(genetic_algorithm)">Selection</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the stage of a&nbsp;<a title="Genetic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_algorithm">genetic algorithm</a>&nbsp;in which individual genomes are chosen from a population for later breeding (using the&nbsp;<a title="Crossover (genetic algorithm)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossover_(genetic_algorithm)">crossover operator</a>).</li>
<li><a title="Self-management (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-management_(computer_science)">Self-management</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process by which&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;systems shall manage their own operation without human intervention.</li>
<li><a title="Semantic network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_network">Semantic network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; or frame network, is a&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge base" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_base">knowledge base</a>&nbsp;that represents&nbsp;<a title="Semantics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantics">semantic</a>&nbsp;relations between&nbsp;<a title="Concept" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concept">concepts</a>&nbsp;in a network. This is often used as a form of&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge representation and reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation_and_reasoning">knowledge representation</a>. It is a&nbsp;<a title="Directed graph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directed_graph">directed</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Undirected graph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undirected_graph">undirected graph</a>&nbsp;consisting of&nbsp;<a title="Vertex (graph theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertex_(graph_theory)">vertices</a>, which represent&nbsp;<a title="Concept" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concept">concepts</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory">edges</a>, which represent&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Semantic relationship" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_relationship">semantic relations</a>&nbsp;between concepts,&nbsp;mapping or connecting&nbsp;<a title="Semantic field" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_field">semantic fields</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Semantic reasoner" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_reasoner">Semantic reasoner</a>&nbsp;&ndash;A semantic reasoner, reasoning engine, rules engine, or simply a reasoner, is a piece of software able to infer&nbsp;<a title="Logical consequence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_consequence">logical consequences</a>&nbsp;from a set of asserted facts or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Axioms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axioms">axioms</a>. The notion of a semantic reasoner generalizes that of an&nbsp;<a title="Inference engine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_engine">inference engine</a>, by providing a richer set of mechanisms to work with. The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Inference rules" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference_rules">inference rules</a>&nbsp;are commonly specified by means of an&nbsp;<a title="Ontology language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontology_language">ontology language</a>, and often a&nbsp;<a title="Description logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Description_logic">description logic</a>&nbsp;language. Many reasoners use&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="First-order predicate logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_predicate_logic">first-order predicate logic</a>&nbsp;to perform reasoning;&nbsp;<a title="Inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference">inference</a>&nbsp;commonly proceeds by&nbsp;<a title="Forward chaining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forward_chaining">forward chaining</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Backward chaining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backward_chaining">backward chaining</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Semantic query" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_query">Semantic query</a>&nbsp;&ndash; allows for queries and analytics of associative and&nbsp;<a title="Contextualization (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contextualization_(computer_science)">contextual</a>&nbsp;nature. Semantic queries enable the retrieval of both explicitly and implicitly derived information based on syntactic, semantic and structural information contained in data. They are designed to deliver precise results (possibly the distinctive selection of one single piece of information) or to answer more fuzzy and wide open questions through&nbsp;<a title="Pattern matching" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_matching">pattern matching</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Reasoning system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning_system">digital reasoning</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Semantics (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantics_(computer_science)">Semantics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Programming language theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language_theory">programming language theory</a>, semantics is the field concerned with the rigorous mathematical study of the meaning of&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming languages</a>. It does so by evaluating the meaning of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Programming language syntax" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language_syntax">syntactically</a>&nbsp;valid&nbsp;<a title="String (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/String_(computer_science)">strings</a>&nbsp;defined by a specific programming language, showing the computation involved. In such a case that the evaluation would be of syntactically invalid strings, the result would be non-computation. Semantics describes the processes a computer follows when executing a program in that specific language. This can be shown by describing the relationship between the input and output of a program, or an explanation of how the program will be executed on a certain&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer platform" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_platform">platform</a>, hence creating a&nbsp;<a title="Model of computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_of_computation">model of computation</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Sensor fusion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensor_fusion">Sensor fusion</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is combining of&nbsp;<a title="Sensor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensor">sensory</a>&nbsp;data or data derived from disparate sources such that the resulting&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>&nbsp;has less uncertainty than would be possible when these sources were used individually.</li>
<li><a title="Separation logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_logic">Separation logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an extension of&nbsp;<a title="Hoare logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoare_logic">Hoare logic</a>, a way of reasoning about programs. The assertion language of separation logic is a special case of the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Logic of bunched implications" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_of_bunched_implications">logic of bunched implications</a>&nbsp;(BI).</li>
<li><a title="Similarity learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Similarity_learning">Similarity learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an area of supervised&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;in artificial intelligence. It is closely related to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Regression (machine learning)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regression_(machine_learning)">regression</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Classification in machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classification_in_machine_learning">classification</a>, but the goal is to learn from a similarity function that measures how similar or related two objects are. It has applications in&nbsp;<a title="Ranking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranking">ranking</a>, in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Recommendation systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recommendation_systems">recommendation systems</a>, visual identity tracking, face verification, and speaker verification.</li>
<li><a title="Simulated annealing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulated_annealing">Simulated annealing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (SA), is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Probabilistic algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilistic_algorithm">probabilistic technique</a>&nbsp;for approximating the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Global optimum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_optimum">global optimum</a>&nbsp;of a given&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>. Specifically, it is a&nbsp;<a title="Metaheuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaheuristic">metaheuristic</a>&nbsp;to approximate&nbsp;<a title="Global optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_optimization">global optimization</a>&nbsp;in a large&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Solution space" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solution_space">search space</a>&nbsp;for an&nbsp;<a title="Optimization problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_problem">optimization problem</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Artificial intelligence, situated approach" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence,_situated_approach">Situated approach</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In artificial intelligence research, the situated approach builds agents that are designed to behave effectively successfully in their environment. This requires designing AI "from the bottom-up" by focussing on the basic perceptual and motor skills required to survive. The situated approach gives a much lower priority to abstract reasoning or problem-solving skills.</li>
<li><a title="Situation calculus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Situation_calculus">Situation calculus</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>&nbsp;formalism designed for representing and reasoning about dynamical domains.</li>
<li><a title="SLD resolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SLD_resolution">SLD resolution</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (<em>Selective Linear Definite</em>&nbsp;clause resolution), is the basic&nbsp;<a title="Rule of inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_inference">inference rule</a>&nbsp;used in&nbsp;<a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">logic programming</a>. It is a refinement of&nbsp;<a title="Resolution (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resolution_(logic)">resolution</a>, which is both&nbsp;<a title="Soundness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soundness">sound</a>&nbsp;and refutation&nbsp;<a title="Completeness (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Completeness_(logic)">complete</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Horn clause" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horn_clause">Horn clauses</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">Software</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Computer software, or simply software, is a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;instructions that tell the computer how to work. This is in contrast to&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">physical hardware</a>, from which the system is built and actually performs the work. In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">software engineering</a>, computer software is all&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>&nbsp;processed by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_system">computer systems</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">programs</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>. Computer software includes&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer programs</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">libraries</a>&nbsp;and related non-executable&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Software documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_documentation">online documentation</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Digital media" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_media">digital media</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">Software engineering</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the application of&nbsp;<a title="Engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering">engineering</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">development</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;in a systematic method.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Spatial-temporal reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spatial-temporal_reasoning">Spatial-temporal reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an area of artificial intelligence which draws from the fields of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science">cognitive science</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive psychology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_psychology">cognitive psychology</a>. The theoretic goal&mdash;on the cognitive side&mdash;involves representing and reasoning spatial-temporal knowledge in mind. The applied goal&mdash;on the computing side&mdash;involves developing high-level control systems of automata for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Robotic navigation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotic_navigation">navigating</a>&nbsp;and understanding time and space.</li>
<li><a title="SPARQL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SPARQL">SPARQL</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="RDF query language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RDF_query_language">RDF query language</a>&mdash;that is, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Semantic Query" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_Query">semantic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Query language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Query_language">query language</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database">databases</a>&mdash;able to retrieve and manipulate data stored in&nbsp;<a title="Resource Description Framework" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework">Resource Description Framework (RDF)</a>&nbsp;format.</li>
<li><a title="Speech recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_recognition">Speech recognition</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interdisciplinary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinary">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Computational linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_linguistics">computational linguistics</a>&nbsp;that develops methodologies and technologies that enables the recognition and&nbsp;<a title="Translation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translation">translation</a>&nbsp;of spoken language into text by computers. It is also known as automatic speech recognition (ASR), computer speech recognition or speech to text (STT). It incorporates knowledge and research in the&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Electrical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_engineering">electrical engineering</a>&nbsp;fields.</li>
<li><a title="Spiking neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spiking_neural_network">Spiking neural network</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (SNNs), are&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neural network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network">artificial neural network</a>s that more closely mimic natural neural networks.&nbsp;In addition to&nbsp;<a title="Artificial neuron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neuron">neuronal</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Electrical synapse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_synapse">synaptic</a>&nbsp;state, SNNs incorporate the concept of time into their&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Operating Model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_Model">operating model</a>.</li>
<li><a title="State (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(computer_science)">State</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Information technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_technology">information technology</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, a program is described as stateful if it is designed to remember preceding events or user interactions;&nbsp;the remembered information is called the state of the system.</li>
<li><a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">Statistical classification</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>, classification is the problem of identifying to which of a set of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Categorical data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Categorical_data">categories</a>&nbsp;(sub-populations) a new&nbsp;<a title="Observation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Observation">observation</a>&nbsp;belongs, on the basis of a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Training set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Training_set">training set</a>&nbsp;of data containing observations (or instances) whose category membership is known. Examples are assigning a given email to the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Spam filtering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spam_filtering">"spam" or "non-spam"</a>&nbsp;class, and assigning a diagnosis to a given patient based on observed characteristics of the patient (sex, blood pressure, presence or absence of certain symptoms, etc.). Classification is an example of&nbsp;<a title="Pattern recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_recognition">pattern recognition</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Statistical relational learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_relational_learning">Statistical relational learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (SRL), is a subdiscipline of artificial intelligence and&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;that is concerned with&nbsp;<a title="Domain model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_model">domain models</a>&nbsp;that exhibit both&nbsp;<a title="Uncertainty" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncertainty">uncertainty</a>&nbsp;(which can be dealt with using statistical methods) and complex,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Relation (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relation_(mathematics)">relational</a>&nbsp;structure.&nbsp;Note that SRL is sometimes called Relational Machine Learning (RML) in the literature. Typically, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">knowledge representation</a>&nbsp;formalisms developed in SRL use (a subset of)&nbsp;<a title="First-order logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-order_logic">first-order logic</a>&nbsp;to describe relational properties of a domain in a general manner (<a title="Universal quantification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_quantification">universal quantification</a>) and draw upon&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Probabilistic graphical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilistic_graphical_model">probabilistic graphical models</a>&nbsp;(such as&nbsp;<a title="Bayesian network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayesian_network">Bayesian networks</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Markov network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_network">Markov networks</a>) to model the uncertainty; some also build upon the methods of&nbsp;<a title="Inductive logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inductive_logic_programming">inductive logic programming</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Stochastic optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_optimization">Stochastic optimization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Stochastic optimization, (SO), methods are&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Optimization (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_(mathematics)">optimization</a>&nbsp;<a title="Iterative method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iterative_method">methods</a>&nbsp;that generate and use&nbsp;<a title="Random variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_variable">random variables</a>. For stochastic problems, the random variables appear in the formulation of the optimization problem itself, which involves random&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Objective function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Objective_function">objective functions</a>&nbsp;or random constraints. Stochastic optimization methods also include methods with random iterates. Some stochastic optimization methods use random iterates to solve stochastic problems, combining both meanings of stochastic optimization.&nbsp;Stochastic optimization methods generalize&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Deterministic system (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deterministic_system_(mathematics)">deterministic</a>&nbsp;methods for deterministic problems.</li>
<li><a title="Stochastic semantic analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_semantic_analysis">Stochastic semantic analysis</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is an approach used in&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Semantic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic">semantic</a>&nbsp;component of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language understanding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_understanding">natural language understanding</a>. Stochastic models generally use the definition of segments of words as basic semantic units for the semantic models, and in some cases involve a two layered approach.</li>
<li><a title="Stanford Research Institute Problem Solver" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_Research_Institute_Problem_Solver">Stanford Research Institute Problem Solver</a>&nbsp;(STRIPS) &ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Automated planning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning">automated planner</a>&nbsp;developed by&nbsp;<a title="Richard Fikes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Fikes">Richard Fikes</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nils Nilsson (researcher)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nils_Nilsson_(researcher)">Nils Nilsson</a>&nbsp;in 1971 at&nbsp;<a title="SRI International" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SRI_International">SRI International</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Subject-matter expert" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subject-matter_expert">Subject-matter expert</a>&nbsp;&ndash; a person who is an authority in a particular area or topic.&nbsp;</li>
<li><a title="Superintelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superintelligence">Superintelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a hypothetical&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">agent</a>&nbsp;that possesses&nbsp;<a title="Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence">intelligence</a>&nbsp;far surpassing that of the&nbsp;<a title="Genius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genius">brightest</a>&nbsp;and most&nbsp;<a title="Intellectual giftedness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intellectual_giftedness">gifted</a>&nbsp;human minds. Superintelligence may also refer to a property of problem-solving systems (e.g., superintelligent language translators or engineering assistants) whether or not these high-level intellectual competencies are embodied in agents that act in the world. A superintelligence may or may not be created by an&nbsp;<a title="Technological singularity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_singularity#Intelligence_explosion">intelligence explosion</a>&nbsp;and associated with a&nbsp;<a title="Technological singularity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_singularity">technological singularity</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning">Supervised learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;task of learning a function that maps an input to an output based on example input-output pairs.&nbsp;It infers a function from&nbsp;<em><span id="LABELLED_DATA"></span><span id="labeled_[[training_set|training_data]]">labeled&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Training set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Training_set">training data</a></span></em>&nbsp;consisting of a set of&nbsp;<em>training examples</em>.&nbsp;In supervised learning, each example is a&nbsp;<em>pair</em>&nbsp;consisting of an input object (typically a vector) and a desired output value (also called the&nbsp;<em>supervisory signal</em>). A supervised learning algorithm analyzes the training data and produces an inferred function, which can be used for mapping new examples. An optimal scenario will allow for the algorithm to correctly determine the class labels for unseen instances. This requires the learning algorithm to generalize from the training data to unseen situations in a "reasonable" way.</li>
<li><a title="Support-vector machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Support-vector_machine">Support-vector machines</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>, support-vector machines (SVMs, also support-vector networks) are&nbsp;<a title="Supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning">supervised learning</a>&nbsp;models with associated learning&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;that analyze data used for&nbsp;<a title="Statistical classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_classification">classification</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Regression analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regression_analysis">regression analysis</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Swarm intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swarm_intelligence">Swarm intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (SI), is the&nbsp;<a title="Collective behavior" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_behavior">collective behavior</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Decentralization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decentralization">decentralized</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Self-organization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-organization">self-organized</a>&nbsp;systems, natural or artificial. The expression was introduced in the context of cellular robotic systems.</li>
<li><a title="Symbolic artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_artificial_intelligence">Symbolic artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the term for the collection of all methods in&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;research that are based on high-level "symbolic" (human-readable) representations of problems,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_logic">logic</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Synthetic intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synthetic_intelligence">Synthetic intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash;(SI), is an alternative term for&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;which emphasizes that the intelligence of machines need not be an imitation or in any way artificial; it can be a genuine form of intelligence.</li>
<li><a title="Systems neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_neuroscience">Systems neuroscience</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a subdiscipline of&nbsp;<a title="Neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Systems biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_biology">systems biology</a>&nbsp;that studies the structure and function of neural circuits and systems. It is an umbrella term, encompassing a number of areas of study concerned with how&nbsp;<a title="Neuron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuron">nerve cells</a>&nbsp;behave when connected together to form&nbsp;<a title="Neural pathway" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_pathway">neural pathways</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Neural circuit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_circuit">neural circuits</a>, and larger&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Large scale brain networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Large_scale_brain_networks">brain networks</a>.</li>
</ul>
<div>&nbsp;</div>
<h2><span id="T" class="mw-headline">T</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Technological singularity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_singularity">Technological singularity</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also, simply, the singularity)&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Hypothetical" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothetical">hypothetical</a>&nbsp;point in the future when technological growth becomes uncontrollable and irreversible, resulting in unfathomable changes to human civilization.</li>
<li><a title="Temporal difference learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temporal_difference_learning">Temporal difference learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (TD) learning refers to a class of&nbsp;<a title="Model-free (reinforcement learning)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model-free_(reinforcement_learning)">model-free</a>&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>&nbsp;methods which learn by&nbsp;<a title="Bootstrapping (statistics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bootstrapping_(statistics)">bootstrapping</a>&nbsp;from the current estimate of the value function. These methods sample from the environment, like&nbsp;<a title="Monte Carlo method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monte_Carlo_method">Monte Carlo methods</a>, and perform updates based on current estimates, like&nbsp;<a title="Dynamic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_programming">dynamic programming</a>&nbsp;methods.</li>
<li><a title="Tensor network theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_network_theory">Tensor network theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a theory of&nbsp;<a title="Brain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain">brain</a>&nbsp;function (particularly that of the&nbsp;<a title="Cerebellum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebellum">cerebellum</a>) that provides a mathematical model of the&nbsp;<a title="Transformation geometry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformation_geometry">transformation</a>&nbsp;of sensory&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Space-time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space-time">space-time</a>&nbsp;coordinates into motor coordinates and vice versa by cerebellar&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Neuronal networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuronal_networks">neuronal networks</a>. The theory was developed as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Geometrization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometrization">geometrization</a>&nbsp;of brain function (especially of the&nbsp;<a title="Central nervous system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_nervous_system">central nervous system</a>) using&nbsp;<a title="Tensor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor">tensors</a>.</li>
<li><a title="TensorFlow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TensorFlow">TensorFlow</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Free software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_software">free</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Open-source software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_software">open-source</a>&nbsp;<a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">software library</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Dataflow programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dataflow_programming">dataflow</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Differentiable programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differentiable_programming">differentiable</a>&nbsp;programming across a range of tasks. It is a symbolic math library, and is also used for&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>&nbsp;applications such as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_networks">neural networks</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">Theoretical computer science</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (TCS), is a subset of general&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;that focuses on more mathematical topics of computing and includes the&nbsp;<a title="Theory of computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_computation">theory of computation</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Theory of computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_computation">Theory of computation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>, the theory of computation is the branch that deals with how efficiently problems can be solved on a&nbsp;<a title="Model of computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_of_computation">model of computation</a>, using an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>. The field is divided into three major branches:&nbsp;<a title="Automata theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automata_theory">automata theory</a>&nbsp;and languages,&nbsp;<a title="Computability theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computability_theory">computability theory</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">computational complexity theory</a>, which are linked by the question:&nbsp;<em>"What are the fundamental capabilities and limitations of computers?".</em></li>
<li><a title="Thompson sampling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thompson_sampling">Thompson sampling</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a heuristic for choosing actions that addresses the exploration-exploitation dilemma in the&nbsp;<a title="Multi-armed bandit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-armed_bandit">multi-armed bandit</a>&nbsp;problem. It consists in choosing the action that maximizes the expected reward with respect to a randomly drawn belief.</li>
<li><a title="Time complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_complexity">Time complexity</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is the&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity">computational complexity</a>&nbsp;that describes the amount of time it takes to run an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>. Time complexity is commonly estimated by counting the number of elementary operations performed by the algorithm, supposing that each elementary operation takes a fixed amount of time to perform. Thus, the amount of time taken and the number of elementary operations performed by the algorithm are taken to differ by at most a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Constant factor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constant_factor">constant factor</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Transhumanism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transhumanism">Transhumanism</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (abbreviated as H+ or h+), is an international&nbsp;<a title="School of thought" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_of_thought">philosophical movement</a>&nbsp;that advocates for the transformation of the&nbsp;<a title="Human condition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_condition">human condition</a>&nbsp;by developing and making widely available sophisticated technologies to greatly&nbsp;<a title="Human enhancement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_enhancement">enhance human</a>&nbsp;intellect and physiology.</li>
<li><a title="Transition system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transition_system">Transition system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>, a transition system is a concept used in the study of&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>. It is used to describe the potential behavior of&nbsp;<a title="Discrete system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_system">discrete systems</a>. It consists of&nbsp;<a title="State (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(computer_science)">states</a>&nbsp;and transitions between states, which may be labeled with labels chosen from a set; the same label may appear on more than one transition. If the label set is a&nbsp;<a title="Singleton (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singleton_(mathematics)">singleton</a>, the system is essentially unlabeled, and a simpler definition that omits the labels is possible.</li>
<li><a title="Tree traversal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_traversal">Tree traversal</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as tree search), is a form of&nbsp;<a title="Graph traversal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_traversal">graph traversal</a>&nbsp;and refers to the process of visiting (checking and/or updating) each node in a&nbsp;<a title="Tree (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_(data_structure)">tree data structure</a>, exactly once. Such traversals are classified by the order in which the nodes are visited.</li>
<li><a title="True quantified Boolean formula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/True_quantified_Boolean_formula">True quantified Boolean formula</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">computational complexity theory</a>, the language TQBF is a&nbsp;<a title="Formal language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_language">formal language</a>&nbsp;consisting of the true quantified Boolean formulas. A (fully) quantified Boolean formula is a formula in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Quantification (logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantification_(logic)">quantified</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Propositional logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propositional_logic">propositional logic</a>&nbsp;where every variable is quantified (or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bound variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bound_variable">bound</a>), using either&nbsp;<a title="Existential quantification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existential_quantification">existential</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Universal quantification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_quantification">universal</a>&nbsp;quantifiers, at the beginning of the sentence. Such a formula is equivalent to either true or false (since there are no&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bound variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bound_variable">free</a>&nbsp;variables). If such a formula evaluates to true, then that formula is in the language TQBF. It is also known as QSAT (Quantified&nbsp;<a title="Boolean satisfiability problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_satisfiability_problem">SAT</a>).</li>
<li><a title="Turing test" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test">Turing test</a>&nbsp;&ndash; developed by&nbsp;<a title="Alan Turing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Turing">Alan Turing</a>&nbsp;in 1950, is a test of a machine's ability to&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">exhibit intelligent behaviour</a>&nbsp;equivalent to, or indistinguishable from, that of a human. Turing proposed that a human evaluator would&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language understanding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_understanding">judge natural language conversations</a>&nbsp;between a human and a machine designed to generate human-like responses. The evaluator would be aware that one of the two partners in conversation is a machine, and all participants would be separated from one another. The conversation would be limited to a text-only channel such as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Keyboard (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keyboard_(computing)">computer keyboard</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Visual display unit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_display_unit">screen</a>&nbsp;so the result would not depend on the machine's ability to render words as speech.&nbsp;If the evaluator cannot reliably tell the machine from the human, the machine is said to have passed the test. The test results do not depend on the machine's ability to give correct answers to questions, only how closely its answers resemble those a human would give.</li>
<li><a title="Type system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_system">Type system</a>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming languages</a>, a type system is a set of rules that assigns a property called&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Type (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_(computer_science)">type</a>&nbsp;to the various constructs of a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Variable (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(computer_science)">variables</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Expression (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(computer_science)">expressions</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Function (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(computer_science)">functions</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Modular programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modular_programming">modules</a>.&nbsp;These types formalize and enforce the otherwise implicit categories the programmer uses for&nbsp;<a title="Algebraic data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_data_type">algebraic data types</a>, data structures, or other components (e.g. "string", "array of float", "function returning boolean"). The main purpose of a type system is to reduce possibilities for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Bug (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bug_(computer_programming)">bugs</a>&nbsp;in computer programs&nbsp;by defining&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interface (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interface_(computer_science)">interfaces</a>&nbsp;between different parts of a computer program, and then checking that the parts have been connected in a consistent way. This checking can happen statically (at&nbsp;<a title="Compile time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compile_time">compile time</a>), dynamically (at&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Run time (program lifecycle phase)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Run_time_(program_lifecycle_phase)">run time</a>), or as a combination of static and dynamic checking. Type systems have other purposes as well, such as expressing business rules, enabling certain compiler optimizations, allowing for&nbsp;<a title="Multiple dispatch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiple_dispatch">multiple dispatch</a>, providing a form of documentation, etc.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="U" class="mw-headline">U</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Unsupervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unsupervised_learning">Unsupervised learning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a type of self-organized&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Hebbian learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebbian_learning">Hebbian learning</a>&nbsp;that helps find previously unknown patterns in data set without pre-existing labels. It is also known as&nbsp;<a title="Self-organization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-organization">self-organization</a>&nbsp;and allows modeling&nbsp;<a title="Probability density function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_density_function">probability densities</a>&nbsp;of given inputs.&nbsp;It is one of the main three categories of machine learning, along with&nbsp;<a title="Supervised learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning">supervised</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Reinforcement learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning">reinforcement learning</a>. Semi-supervised learning has also been described and is a hybridization of supervised and unsupervised techniques.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="V" class="mw-headline">V</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Vision processing unit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vision_processing_unit">Vision processing unit</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (VPU), is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Microprocessor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microprocessor">microprocessor</a>&nbsp;designed to&nbsp;<a title="Hardware acceleration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardware_acceleration">accelerate</a>&nbsp;<a title="Machine vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_vision">machine vision</a>&nbsp;tasks.</li>
<li><span class="citation-needed-content">Value-alignment complete &ndash; Analogous to an&nbsp;<a title="AI-complete" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI-complete">AI-complete</a>&nbsp;problem, a value-alignment complete problem is a problem where the&nbsp;<a title="AI control problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_control_problem">AI control problem</a>&nbsp;needs to be fully solved to solve it.</span></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="W" class="mw-headline">W</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Watson (computer)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watson_(computer)">Watson</a>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Question answering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Question_answering">question-answering</a>&nbsp;computer system capable of answering questions posed in&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural language</a>,&nbsp;developed in&nbsp;<a title="IBM" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM">IBM</a>'s DeepQA project by a research team led by&nbsp;<a title="Principal investigator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principal_investigator">principal investigator</a>&nbsp;<a title="David Ferrucci" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ferrucci">David Ferrucci</a>.&nbsp;Watson was named after IBM's first CEO, industrialist&nbsp;<a title="Thomas J. Watson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_J._Watson">Thomas J. Watson</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Weak AI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_AI">Weak AI</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (weak AI), also known as narrow AI,&nbsp;is&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;that is focused on one narrow task.</li>
<li><a title="World Wide Web Consortium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium</a>&nbsp;&ndash; (W3C), is the main international&nbsp;<a title="Standards organization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standards_organization">standards organization</a>&nbsp;for the&nbsp;<a title="World Wide Web" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web">World Wide Web</a>&nbsp;(abbreviated WWW or W3).</li>
</ul>
</br>

<h2 id ="Branches">The Most Significant Failures When Al Turned Rogue, Causing Disastrous Results </h2>

<ul>
<li><strong>1959:</strong> AI designed to be a General Problem Solver failed to solve real world problems.</li>
<li><strong>1982:</strong> Software designed to make discoveries, discovered how to cheat instead.</li>
<li><strong>1983:</strong> Nuclear attack early warning system falsely claimed that an attack is taking place.</li>
<li><strong>2010:</strong> Complex AI stock trading software caused a trillion dollar flash crash.</li>
<li><strong>2011:</strong> E-Assistant told to "call me an ambulance" began to refer to the user as Ambulance.</li>
<li><strong>2013:</strong> Object recognition neural networks saw phantom objects in particular noise images.</li>
<li><strong>2015:</strong> An automated email reply generator created inappropriate responses, such as writing "I love you" to a business colleague.</li>
<li><strong>2015:</strong> A robot for grabbing auto parts grabbed and killed a man.</li>
<li><strong>2015:</strong> Image tagging software classified black people as gorillas.</li>
<li><strong>2015:</strong> Medical AI classified patients with asthma as having a lower risk of dying of pneumonia.</li>
<li><strong>2015:</strong> Adult content filtering software failed to remove inappropriate content, exposing children to violent and sexual content.</li>
<li><strong>2016:</strong> AI designed to predict recidivism acted racist.&nbsp;</li>
<li><strong> 2016:</strong> An AI agent exploited a reward signal to win a game without actually completing the game.</li>
<li><strong>2016:</strong> Video game NPCs (non-player characters, or any character that is not controlled by a human player) designed unauthorized super weapons.</li>
<li><strong>2016:</strong> AI judged a beauty contest and rated dark-skinned contestants lower.</li>
<li><strong>2016:</strong> A mall security robot collided with and injured a child.</li>
<li><strong>2016:</strong> The AI "Alpha Go" lost to a human in a world-championship-level game of "Go."</li>
<li><strong>2016:</strong> A self-driving car had a deadly accident.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Google Translate shows gender bias in Turkish-English translations.&nbsp;</li>
<li><strong> 2017:</strong> Facebook chat bots shut down after developing their own language.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Autonomous van in accident on its first day.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Google Allo suggested man in turban emoji as response to a gun emoji.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Face ID beat by a mask.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> AI misses the mark with Kentucky Derby predictions.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Google Home Minis spied on their owners.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Google Home outage causes near 100% failure rate.</li>
<li><strong>2017:</strong> Facebook allowed ads to be targeted to "Jew Haters".</li>
<li><strong>2018:</strong> Chinese billionaire's face identified as jaywalker.</li>
<li><strong>2018:</strong> Uber self-driving car kills a pedestrian.</li>
<li><strong>2018:</strong> Amazon AI recruiting tool is gender biased.</li>
<li><strong>2018:</strong> Google Photo confuses skier and mountain.</li>
<li><strong>2018:</strong> LG robot Cloi gets stagefright at its unveiling.</li>
<li><strong>2018:</strong> IBM Watson comes up short in healthcare.</li>
</ul>


<p>While these are only a few instances of failures that have been observed so far, they are pieces of evidence to the fact that Artificial intelligence (the simulation of human intelligence processes by machines, especially computer systems) has the potential to develop a will of its own that may be in conflict with members of the human race. This is definitely a warning about the potential dangers of Artificial intelligence which should be addressed while exploring its potential interests.</p>
<p>Artificial intelligence in general, context remains a challenge. Despite Its Many Failures, why is artificial intelligence important?</p>
<ul>
<li>Artificial intelligence automates repetitive learning and discovery through data.</li>
<li>Artificial intelligence analyzes more and deeper data.</li>
<li>Artificial intelligence adds intelligence to existing products.</li>
<li>Artificial intelligence adapts through progressive learning algorithms to let the data do the programming.</li>
<li>Artificial intelligence gets the most out of data.</li>
<li>Artificial intelligence achieves unbelievable accuracy through deep neural networks &ndash; which was previously impossible. For example, your interactions with Amazon Alexa, Google Search and Google Photos are all based on deep learning &ndash; and they keep getting more precise the more we use them.</li>
</ul>
<p>The threat of AI-charged job loss is spreading (AI and automation will eliminate the most mundane tasks). No matter what industry you&rsquo;re in, AI-powered bots (which can answer common questions and point users to FAQs and knowledge base articles) and software are taking a crack at it. Artificial intelligence seems to be ringing the death sound of a bell for all manner of jobs, tasks, chores and activities. From hospitality, to customer service, to home assistants, no job feels safe. Naturally, this has made people worried about the future. But is Artificial intelligence ready to take over our jobs, or even likely to do so ever? <strong>Prevalent AI- charged failures</strong> would suggest not.</p>

</br>
