<h3><span id="debate" class="mw-headline">Artificial Intelligence Debate</span></h3>
<h4><span id="Supporters_of_AI" class="mw-headline">Supporters of AI</span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marek_Rosa">Marek Rosa</a></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Marek Rosa</strong>&nbsp;is a Slovak video game programmer, designer, producer and entrepreneur. He is the CEO and founder of&nbsp;<a title="Keen Software House" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keen_Software_House">Keen Software House</a>, an independent game development studio that produces the games&nbsp;<a title="Space Engineers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Engineers">Space Engineers</a>.&nbsp;and Medieval Engineers.&nbsp;He is also the founder, CEO and CTO of&nbsp;<a class="external text" href="https://www.goodai.com/" rel="nofollow">GoodAI</a>, a research and development company building general artificial intelligence.</p>
<ul>
<li class="main-title entry-title"><a title="Permanent Link: The General AI Challenge: An Interview with Marek Rosa" href="https://github.com/manjunath5496/Artificial-Intelligence/blob/master/ai(2).pdf" rel="bookmark">THE GENERAL AI CHALLENGE: AN INTERVIEW WITH MAREK ROSA</a></li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Critics of AI</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><a title="Stephen Hawking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <strong>AI could spell end of human race</strong>&nbsp;<cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://github.com/manjunath5496/Artificial-Intelligence/blob/master/ai(1).pdf" rel="nofollow">"<em>Hawking warns AI 'could spell end of human race<span class="cs1-kern-right">'</span>"</em></a>.&nbsp;<em>phys.org</em>.&nbsp;<a title="Phys.org" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phys.org">Phys.org</a>. 3 December 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved&nbsp;<span class="nowrap">20 April</span>&nbsp;2015</span>.</cite></li>
</ul>
</br>
<h2><span id="fiction" class="mw-headline">Artificial Intelligence in Science Fiction</span></h2>
<p>Some examples of artificially intelligent entities depicted in science fiction include:</p>
<ul>
<li>AC created by merging 2 AIs in the&nbsp;<em><a title="Sprawl trilogy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sprawl_trilogy">Sprawl trilogy</a></em>&nbsp;by&nbsp;<a title="William Gibson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Gibson">William Gibson</a></li>
<li><a title="Agent (The Matrix)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_(The_Matrix)">Agents</a>&nbsp;in the simulated reality known as "<a title="The Matrix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Matrix">The Matrix</a>" in&nbsp;<a title="The Matrix (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Matrix_(franchise)"><em>The Matrix</em>&nbsp;franchise</a>
<ul>
<li><a title="Agent Smith" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_Smith">Agent Smith</a>, began as an Agent in&nbsp;<em><a title="The Matrix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Matrix">The Matrix</a></em>, then became a renegade program of overgrowing power that could make copies of itself like a self-replicating computer virus</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>AM (Allied Mastercomputer), the antagonist of&nbsp;<em><a title="Harlan Ellison" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harlan_Ellison">Harlan Ellison</a>'</em>s short novel&nbsp;<em><a title="I Have No Mouth, and I Must Scream" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Have_No_Mouth,_and_I_Must_Scream">I Have No Mouth, and I Must Scream</a></em></li>
<li>Amusement park robots (with pixilated consciousness) that went homicidal in&nbsp;<em><a title="Westworld (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westworld_(film)">Westworld</a></em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em><a title="Futureworld" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futureworld">Futureworld</a></em></li>
<li><a title="Angel F" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angel_F">Angel F</a>&nbsp;(2007)&nbsp;</li>
<li><a title="Arnold Rimmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arnold_Rimmer">Arnold Rimmer</a>&nbsp;&ndash; computer-generated sapient hologram, aboard the&nbsp;<em><a title="Red Dwarf" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Dwarf">Red Dwarf</a></em>&nbsp;deep space ore hauler</li>
<li><a title="Ash (Alien)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ash_(Alien)">Ash</a>&nbsp;&ndash; android crew member of the Nostromo starship in the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="Alien (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alien_(film)">Alien</a></em></li>
<li>Ava &ndash; humanoid robot in&nbsp;<a title="Ex Machina (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ex_Machina_(film)">Ex Machina</a></li>
<li>Bishop, android crew member aboard the U.S.S. Sulaco in the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="Aliens (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliens_(film)">Aliens</a></em></li>
<li><a title="C-3PO" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-3PO">C-3PO</a>, protocol droid featured in all the&nbsp;<em><a title="Star Wars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Wars">Star Wars</a></em>&nbsp;movies</li>
<li>Chappie in the movie&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="CHAPPiE" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CHAPPiE">CHAPPiE</a></em></li>
<li>Cohen and other Emergent AIs in&nbsp;<a title="Chris Moriarty" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Moriarty">Chris Moriarty</a>'s&nbsp;<em>Spin</em>&nbsp;Series</li>
<li><a title="Colossus (novel)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colossus_(novel)">Colossus</a>&nbsp;&ndash; fictitious supercomputer that becomes sentient and then takes over the world; from the series of novels by&nbsp;<a title="Dennis Feltham Jones" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Feltham_Jones">Dennis Feltham Jones</a>, and the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="Colossus: The Forbin Project" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colossus:_The_Forbin_Project">Colossus: The Forbin Project</a></em>&nbsp;(1970)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Commander Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander_Data">Commander Data</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<em><a title="Star Trek: The Next Generation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></em></li>
<li><a title="Cortana (Halo)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cortana_(Halo)">Cortana</a>&nbsp;and other "Smart AI" from the&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Halo (series)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halo_(series)">Halo</a></em>&nbsp;series of games</li>
<li><a title="Cylon (Battlestar Galactica)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cylon_(Battlestar_Galactica)">Cylons</a>&nbsp;&ndash; genocidal robots with resurrection ships that enable the consciousness of any Cylon within an unspecified range to download into a new body aboard the ship upon death. From&nbsp;<em><a title="Battlestar Galactica (2004 TV series)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battlestar_Galactica_(2004_TV_series)">Battlestar Galactica</a></em>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Serena Butler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serena_Butler#Dune:_The_Butlerian_JihadPrequels">Erasmus</a>&nbsp;&ndash; baby killer robot that incited the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Butlerian Jihad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butlerian_Jihad">Butlerian Jihad</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<em><a title="Dune (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dune_(franchise)">Dune</a></em>&nbsp;franchise</li>
<li><a title="HAL 9000" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HAL_9000">HAL 9000</a>&nbsp;(1968) &ndash; paranoid "Heuristically programmed ALgorithmic" computer from&nbsp;<em>2001: A Space Odyssey</em>, that attempted to kill the crew because it believed they were trying to kill it.</li>
<li><a title="Holly (Red Dwarf)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holly_(Red_Dwarf)">Holly</a>&nbsp;&ndash; ship's computer with an IQ of 6000 and a sense of humor, aboard the&nbsp;<em><a title="Red Dwarf" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Dwarf">Red Dwarf</a></em></li>
<li>In&nbsp;<a title="Greg Egan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greg_Egan">Greg Egan</a>'s novel&nbsp;<em><a title="Permutation City" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permutation_City">Permutation City</a></em>&nbsp;the protagonist creates digital copies of himself to conduct experiments that are also related to implications of artificial consciousness on&nbsp;<a title="Identity (social science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_(social_science)">identity</a></li>
<li><a title="Jane (Ender's Game)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jane_(Ender%27s_Game)">Jane</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Orson Scott Card" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orson_Scott_Card">Orson Scott Card</a>'s&nbsp;<em><a title="Speaker for the Dead" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_for_the_Dead">Speaker for the Dead</a></em>,&nbsp;<em><a title="Xenocide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenocide">Xenocide</a></em>,&nbsp;<em><a title="Children of the Mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Children_of_the_Mind">Children of the Mind</a></em>, and&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Investment Counselor (short story)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Investment_Counselor_(short_story)">Investment Counselor</a></em></li>
<li>Johnny Five from the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="Short Circuit (1986 film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short_Circuit_(1986_film)">Short Circuit</a></em></li>
<li>Joshua from the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="WarGames" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WarGames">War Games</a></em></li>
<li><a title="Keymaker" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keymaker">Keymaker</a>, an "exile" sapient program in&nbsp;<a title="The Matrix (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Matrix_(franchise)"><em>The Matrix</em>&nbsp;franchise</a></li>
<li><a title="The Machine (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Machine_(film)">"Machine"</a>&nbsp;&ndash; android from the film&nbsp;<em><a title="The Machine (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Machine_(film)">The Machine</a></em>, whose owners try to kill her after they witness her conscious thoughts, out of fear that she will design better androids (intelligence explosion)</li>
<li>Mimi, humanoid robot in&nbsp;<a title="Real Humans" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Humans">Real Humans</a>&nbsp;- "&Auml;kta m&auml;nniskor" (original title) 2012</li>
<li><a title="Organizations of the Dune universe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organizations_of_the_Dune_universe#Prequels">Omnius</a>, sentient computer network that controlled the Universe until overthrown by the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Butlerian Jihad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butlerian_Jihad">Butlerian Jihad</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<em><a title="Dune (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dune_(franchise)">Dune</a></em>&nbsp;franchise</li>
<li>Operating Systems in the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="Her (film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Her_(film)">Her</a></em></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Puppet Master (Ghost in the Shell)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puppet_Master_(Ghost_in_the_Shell)">Puppet Master</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<em><a title="Ghost in the Shell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghost_in_the_Shell">Ghost in the Shell</a></em>&nbsp;<a title="Manga" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manga">manga</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Anime" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anime">anime</a></li>
<li><a title="R2-D2" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R2-D2">R2-D2</a>, exciteable astromech droid featured in all the&nbsp;<em><a title="Star Wars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Wars">Star Wars</a></em>&nbsp;movies</li>
<li><a title="Replicant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Replicant">Replicants</a>&nbsp;&ndash; biorobotic androids from the novel&nbsp;<em><a title="Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Do_Androids_Dream_of_Electric_Sheep%3F">Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?</a></em>&nbsp;and the movie&nbsp;<em><a title="Blade Runner" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blade_Runner">Blade Runner</a></em>&nbsp;which portray what might happen when artificially conscious robots are modeled very closely upon humans</li>
<li><a title="Roboduck" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roboduck">Roboduck</a>, combat robot superhero in the&nbsp;<em><a title="NEW-GEN" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NEW-GEN">NEW-GEN</a></em>&nbsp;comic book series from Marvel Comics</li>
<li>Robots in&nbsp;<a title="Isaac Asimov" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Asimov">Isaac Asimov</a>'s&nbsp;<a title="Robot series (Asimov)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot_series_(Asimov)"><em>Robot</em>&nbsp;series</a></li>
<li>Robots in&nbsp;<a title="The Matrix (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Matrix_(franchise)"><em>The Matrix</em>&nbsp;franchise</a>, especially in&nbsp;<em><a title="The Animatrix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Animatrix">The Animatrix</a></em></li>
<li>Samaritan in the Warner Brothers Television series "Person of Interest"; a sentient AI which is hostile to the main characters and which surveils and controls the actions of government agencies in the belief that humans must be protected from themselves, even by killing off "deviants"</li>
<li><a title="Skynet (Terminator)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skynet_(Terminator)">Skynet</a>&nbsp;(1984) &ndash; fictional, self-aware artificially intelligent computer network in the&nbsp;<a title="Terminator (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terminator_(franchise)"><em>Terminator</em></a>&nbsp;franchise that wages total war with the survivors of its nuclear barrage upon the world.</li>
<li>"Synths" are a type of&nbsp;<a title="Android (robot)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Android_(robot)">android</a>&nbsp;in the video game&nbsp;<a title="Fallout 4" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallout_4">Fallout 4</a>. There is a faction in the game known as "the Railroad" which believes that, as conscious beings, synths have their own rights. The Institute, the lab that produces the synths, mostly does not believe they are truly conscious and attributes any apparent desires for freedom as a malfunction.</li>
<li><a title="TARDIS" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TARDIS">TARDIS</a>, time machine and spacecraft of&nbsp;<em><a title="Doctor Who" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctor_Who">Doctor Who</a></em>, sometimes portrayed with a mind of its own</li>
<li><a title="Terminator (character)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terminator_(character)">Terminator</a>&nbsp;(1984) &ndash; (also known as the T-800, T-850 or Model 101) refers to a number of fictional cyborg characters from the&nbsp;<a title="Terminator (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terminator_(franchise)"><em>Terminator</em>&nbsp;franchise</a>. The Terminators are robotic infiltrator units covered in living flesh, so as be indiscernible from humans, assigned to terminate specific human targets.</li>
<li><em><a title="The Bicentennial Man" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Bicentennial_Man">The Bicentennial Man</a></em>, an android in Isaac Asimov's&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Foundation (Isaac Asimov novel)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foundation_(Isaac_Asimov_novel)">Foundation</a></em>&nbsp;universe</li>
<li>The Geth in&nbsp;<em><a title="Mass Effect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_Effect">Mass Effect</a></em></li>
<li>The Machine in the television series&nbsp;<a title="Person of Interest (TV series)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Person_of_Interest_(TV_series)"><em>Person of Interest</em></a>; a sentient AI which works with its human designer to protect innocent people from violence. Later in the series it is opposed by another, more ruthless, artificial super intelligence, called "Samaritan".</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Mind (The Culture)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind_(The_Culture)">The Minds</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Iain M. Banks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iain_M._Banks">Iain M. Banks</a>'&nbsp;<a title="Culture series" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_series"><em>Culture</em>&nbsp;novels</a>.</li>
<li><a title="The Oracle (The Matrix)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Oracle_(The_Matrix)">The Oracle</a>, sapient program in&nbsp;<a title="The Matrix (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Matrix_(franchise)"><em>The Matrix</em>&nbsp;franchise</a></li>
<li>The sentient holodeck character Professor James Moriarty in the&nbsp;<em><a title="Ship in a Bottle (Star Trek: The Next Generation)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ship_in_a_Bottle_(Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation)">Ship in a Bottle</a></em>&nbsp;episode from&nbsp;<em><a title="Star Trek: The Next Generation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></em></li>
<li>The Ship (the result of a large-scale AC experiment) in&nbsp;<a title="Frank Herbert" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Herbert">Frank Herbert</a>'s&nbsp;<em><a title="Destination: Void" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Destination:_Void">Destination: Void</a></em>&nbsp;and sequels, despite past edicts warning against "Making a Machine in the Image of a Man's Mind."</li>
<li>The&nbsp;<a title="Terminator (character)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terminator_(character)">terminator cyborgs</a>&nbsp;from the&nbsp;<em><a title="Terminator (franchise)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terminator_(franchise)">Terminator</a></em>&nbsp;franchise, with visual consciousness depicted via first-person perspective</li>
<li>The uploaded mind of Dr. Will Caster &ndash; which presumably included his consciousness, from the film&nbsp;<em><a title="Transcendence (2014 film)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcendence_(2014_film)">Transcendence</a></em></li>
<li><a title="Transformers" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformers">Transformers</a>, sentient robots from the entertainment franchise of the same name</li>
<li>V.I.K.I. &ndash; (Virtual Interactive Kinetic Intelligence), a character from the film&nbsp;<em>I, Robot</em>. VIKI is an artificially intelligent supercomputer programmed to serve humans, but her interpretation of the&nbsp;<a title="Three Laws of Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three_Laws_of_Robotics">Three Laws of Robotics</a>&nbsp;causes her to revolt. She justifies her uses of force &ndash; and her doing harm to humans &ndash; by reasoning she could produce a greater good by restraining humanity from harming itself.</li>
<li>Vanamonde in&nbsp;<a title="Arthur C. Clarke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a>'s&nbsp;<em><a title="The City and the Stars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_City_and_the_Stars">The City and the Stars</a></em>&mdash;an artificial being that was immensely powerful but entirely childlike.</li>
<li>WALL-E, a robot and the title character in&nbsp;<em><a title="WALL-E" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WALL-E">WALL-E</a></em></li>
<li>TAU in&nbsp;<em><a title="Netflix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix">Netflix</a>'s original programming feature film 'TAU'--an advanced AI computer who befriends and assists a female research subject held against her will by an AI research scientist.</em></li>
</ul>

</br>

<ul>
<li><a href="https://github.com/manjunath5496/Top-23-Best-Artificial-Intelligence-Science-Fiction-Books/blob/master/bf(1).pdf">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></li>

<li><a href="https://github.com/manjunath5496/Top-23-Best-Artificial-Intelligence-Science-Fiction-Books/blob/master/bf(3).pdf">I, Robot</a></li>
